{"type":"queue-operation","operation":"enqueue","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:13.817Z","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","content":"hi my friend, M1.2 is finished and merge and i was about to to go m1.3 but adrs are not righ we need to introduce mode features, below is my discussion with you on another session, check it out, read ADRS and code base and lets discuss \n\nwhat m 1.3 asks?\n\n\nRan 2 commands, searched code, read a file\nM1.3 isn't in a dedicated plan file yet — it'll be authored when we start the next milestone. But the M1.2 plan has scattered forward-references that make the scope pretty clear. From docs/execution-plan.md §M1 and the M1.2 deferrals/PI tables:\n\nM1.3 — 2D Editor Shell\n\nNew packages: packages/editor-2d (canvas paint loop, no React), packages/ui-state (selection, active tool, viewport as a separate store).\nCanvas: minimal 2D canvas that subscribes directly to projectStore (vanilla) — no @portplanner/project-store-react. The GU.2 canvas-no-React grep gate activates here.\nFirst real mutations: placeObject, moveObject, etc. — these are the first actions that emit Operations into the log per ADR-010 (M1.2 deferred emission as PI-1).\nCoordinate system UI (PI-2): New Project dialog (or a separate step) gains origin lat/lng + true-north rotation + UTM-zone inputs. M1.3 enforces coordinateSystem !== null before any object can be placed.\nCoordinateSystem transforms: toProjectLocal, toWGS84, projectLocalToMapPixel, mapPixelToProjectLocal — class behaviour (M1.2 only stored the data).\nUndo/redo in anger: Ctrl+Z / Ctrl+Shift+Z shortcuts wired to projectStore.temporal, now that there are real mutations to revert.\nWhat's still deferred past M1.3:\n\nRTG_BLOCK-specific geometry + config dialog + extraction (that's M1.4)\n3D viewer (M5)\nValidation engine (probably M1.4 alongside RTG_BLOCK)\nSo M1.3 is essentially: give the store something to mutate, render those mutations on a canvas, let the user undo them. After that M1.4 glues the first real object type (RTG_BLOCK) onto this machinery and M1 is done.\n\nIf/when you want to start M1.3, open a fresh session, point it at docs/procedures/Claude/01-plan-authoring.md + this summary, and it can draft the plan cold.\n\nwould it make sense to define primitives there, line polyline rectangle circle too, as well as osnap otrack and polar, what to you think?\n\nHonest answer: partially, and it depends on a deeper question that's worth naming before you commit to it.\n\nLet me separate the two questions in what you asked:\n\n1) Generic primitives (line, polyline, rectangle, circle)\nMy recommendation: no — not as M1.3 scope. Two reasons:\n\na) They're not in the data model. ADR-002 says PortPlanner stores typed objects (RTG_BLOCK, ROAD, BUILDING, PAVEMENT…), not primitives. An RTG_BLOCK isn't \"a rectangle + some labels\"; it's an object with { width, length, rows, columns, orientation, ... } whose footprint happens to be rectangular. The extractor reads those parameters, not a generic geometry blob.\n\nIf you add primitives as drawable things, you've introduced a second data layer that lives alongside objects but doesn't extract, doesn't validate, doesn't participate in scenarios. That's a real architectural choice, not a small addition — worth its own ADR, and worth asking whether the app is \"object-model editor\" (current architecture) or \"CAD tool where you compose objects from primitives\" (what primitives would imply).\n\nb) The execution-plan principle is explicit: \"Ship a closed loop end-to-end before widening the feature set.\" M1's whole point is one object type, end-to-end. Adding a primitives layer widens the feature set before the loop closes.\n\nIf you want a construction-line / reference-geometry layer later (non-extracted, purely for visual guidance while drawing), that's legit — but it's M2+ and needs its own ADR. Keep it off M1.3.\n\n2) OSNAP / OTRACK / POLAR\nThese are different — they're tool-layer infrastructure, not data-layer. They don't change the object model; they change how the cursor behaves during drawing. They apply equally well whether you're placing an RTG_BLOCK, a road, or a building.\n\nMy recommendation:\n\nAid\tM1.3?\tWhy\nOSNAP (endpoint / midpoint / center / intersection / grid-snap)\tYes, basic set\tPlacing an RTG_BLOCK rectangle will feel broken without at least grid-snap + endpoint-snap. Worth building into the tool system once, since RTG_BLOCK in M1.4 and every later object type will reuse it.\nPOLAR (axis-lock / ortho, 45°/90°/custom angle lock)\tYes, minimal\tOrtho (hold Shift) is cheap. Full polar-tracking at N angles is heavier — defer that part.\nOTRACK (object snap tracking — alignment lines from other objects' snap points)\tNo — defer\tExpensive to implement well (alignment line resolution, multi-source tracking). Not needed for RTG_BLOCK-only M1. Lands in M2 when multiple object types start coexisting and alignment between them matters.\nThe general rule: tool-layer infrastructure that any future object type will reuse is good M1.3 scope, because the canvas exists there for the first time and retrofitting snap systems later is expensive. Data-layer features that aren't part of the object model (generic primitives) are not.\n\nWhat I'd actually put in M1.3\npackages/editor-2d with canvas + view transform + tool-system skeleton\npackages/ui-state (selection / active tool / viewport)\nCoordinateSystem UI (PI-2 from M1.2) — origin + rotation + UTM zone\nOSNAP infrastructure (grid + endpoint at minimum; hooks so more snap types plug in)\nOrtho / axis-lock modifier (Shift-to-constrain)\nFirst real mutation actions (placeObject, moveObject) emitting Operations per ADR-010\nCtrl+Z / Ctrl+Shift+Z wired to projectStore.temporal\nThat's a lot already — probably more than one milestone's worth. The snap/polar infrastructure is the item most likely to get cut and deferred to M1.4 under time pressure, but I'd argue against that; you'll regret it.\n\nThe meta-point\nThe question \"should the editor be object-first or primitive-first\" deserves an explicit architectural answer before you start M1.3. It's the kind of decision that quietly shapes everything downstream. If you want, when you start M1.3, first pass could be an ADR draft: \"ADR-016 — Drawing model: typed-object placement, not primitive composition\" (or the inverse, if you want to rethink). That locks the answer and removes the recurring temptation.\n\nthat is definately a gap in ADR that i want to change and i will discuss it then in new session, but esentially, i want to have those primities ( forgot one which is xline, like CAD has) and as well i want a layer management system. i need dimension lines too. \nidea is to be able to define some objest two fold - by converting primitives to them (line and polyline to roads, fencing), lines to rtg, and roads too(for now, later ill expand its use case ), rectangle to paving buildings...\ni understnad this is not ADR prescribed but this is the time to fix it\n\nThat's a significant and correct architectural move. It's not a detail — it's a shift in the data model, and this is genuinely the right time to make it, before M1.3 commits the canvas to one shape or the other. Here's how I'd frame it for the new session.\n\nWhat you're actually proposing\nA hybrid data model where the project contains two kinds of first-class entities:\n\nPrimitives (line, polyline, xline, rectangle, circle, possibly arc) — persistent CAD-style geometry with a layer, linetype, color, etc.\nTyped objects (RTG_BLOCK, ROAD, BUILDING, PAVEMENT, FENCE…) — same as ADR-002 today.\nWith a promotion path between them: a primitive (or set of primitives) can be converted into a typed object, given some additional parameters the primitive alone can't express.\n\nPlus cross-cutting infrastructure: layers, dimensions, snap system. This is essentially saying PortPlanner is a CAD tool that happens to produce extractable port-yard objects, not a structured editor that happens to render some shapes. Very different posture.\n\nDecisions to land in the ADR (not now — in the new session)\nThese are the questions the ADR has to answer explicitly. Bring them into the new session with your preferences:\n\n1. Primitive persistence: first-class or construction-only?\nFirst-class (my read of what you want): lines/polylines/rectangles are saved forever, can be drawn and left alone, can be promoted later or never.\nConstruction-only: primitives are scaffolding that a promotion consumes; the saved file only contains typed objects.\nFirst-class matches real CAD workflows and matches what you described (\"define objects two-fold\"). Go with first-class.\n\n2. What happens to a primitive on promotion?\nThree options, pick one:\n\nConsume: line → RTG_BLOCK; line is gone.\nPreserve: line stays, RTG_BLOCK is created alongside it.\nBind: RTG_BLOCK references the line as its geometry source; editing the line edits the block's footprint; deleting the line orphans the block.\n\"Bind\" is powerful but expensive — it turns objects into views over primitives, breaks ADR-002's \"object owns its geometry\" assumption, and complicates extraction (extractor now has to resolve references). I'd recommend consume for M1, with a field on the object remembering \"I was born from a polyline\" for audit/undo, but no live link. Revisit live binding in M2+.\n\n3. What parameters must the promotion dialog collect?\nPer conversion, declared in the extraction registry. E.g.:\n\nline → RTG_BLOCK: user draws the travel-axis centerline. Dialog collects rows, columns, block width, TEU height, twinlift/single, etc. Line length determines block length.\nrectangle → BUILDING: dialog collects building type, floors, height. Rectangle gives footprint.\npolyline → ROAD: dialog collects lane count, direction, speed class. Polyline is the centerline.\npolyline → FENCE: dialog collects fence type, gate openings.\nThis is a new column in the extraction registry: \"constructors\" — ordered list of (primitive shape → parameters required). An object type can have multiple constructors (line OR polyline for roads, in your example).\n\n4. Layers: data-layer or view-layer?\nMy recommendation: data-layer, light.\n\nEvery entity (primitive, object, dimension) has layerId: LayerId.\nLayers persist in the project file with { id, name, color, linetype, visible, locked }.\nLayer affects visibility and drawing style, NOT extraction. Extraction is layer-agnostic — an RTG_BLOCK on layer \"hidden\" still extracts.\nNo layer-state management (AutoCAD LSM). Keep it simple.\n5. Dimensions: associative-annotative, not parametric.\nDimension reads geometry; does NOT drive it.\nDimension is its own entity type with a layer, style, and references to the measured points/edges.\nOn geometry edit, dimension updates automatically (it's a function of its references).\nThis is dramatically simpler than parametric/driving dimensions, and it's what 99% of CAD-adjacent use cases need.\n6. Undo / operation log: does Operation cover primitives too?\nYes, has to. ADR-010 extends: Operation.targetKind: 'object' | 'primitive' | 'dimension' | 'layer'. Every primitive mutation emits, same as objects. Single ordered log, same sync model.\n\nThe ADRs you'll need\nI'd propose this breakdown (agree/modify in the new session):\n\nADR\tCovers\nADR-016 Drawing model\tHybrid primitive+object; first-class primitives; promotion contract; list of supported primitive types (line, polyline, xline, rectangle, circle; arc TBD)\nADR-002 revision or ADR-017\tUpdate object model: objects have a sourceKind: 'direct' | 'promoted-from-primitive' provenance field; conversion contract registered in extraction registry\nADR-018 Layer model\tLayers as data-layer light; no layer-state-management; layer does not affect extraction\nADR-019 Dimensions\tAssociative-annotative only; own entity type; references-based, updates with geometry\nADR-010 amendment\tOperation.targetKind extended to cover primitive/dimension/layer\nExtraction registry schema bump\tNew constructors column listing primitive-based creation paths per object type\nWhat changes about M1.3 scope\nMuch larger than my previous answer. The new M1.3 now has to include:\n\npackages/editor-2d canvas + view transform + tool system\npackages/ui-state (selection, active tool, viewport, active layer)\nPrimitive data model in packages/domain (line, polyline, xline, rectangle, circle) — each with its own type + schema + serializer support\nLayer data model in packages/domain\nDimension data model in packages/domain (or defer to M1.4 if too heavy)\nPrimitive draw tools (one per primitive)\nOSNAP + ortho + basic polar — these are now load-bearing, not nice-to-have\nCoordinateSystem UI (carry from M1.2 deferral)\nOperation log actually emitting (first real mutations exist now)\nUndo/redo shortcuts\nThat's maybe 2–3 weeks of work. Might break into M1.3a (domain + canvas + primitives + snap) and M1.3b (layers + dimensions + promotion to RTG_BLOCK), with M1.4 becoming \"RTG_BLOCK extraction + validation + yard capacity panel.\"\n\nMy honest reaction\nThis is a better architecture than the pure typed-object model, for the domain you're in. Port planning is a CAD-adjacent activity; the people who'll use this tool think in lines, polylines, layers, and dimensions natively. Forcing them into \"click the RTG tool, click two points\" without letting them draft freely first is going to feel rigid. The hybrid model matches the user's mental model.\n\nDownsides to go in open-eyed:\n\nM1 goalposts move — you won't close the end-to-end loop as fast as the current M1 plan implies.\nMore ADRs to maintain. More surface area to review.\nPromotion contract is subtle — get it wrong and you either get (a) lossy conversions where info is dropped, or (b) zombie primitives that nobody owns.\nSnap + ortho + polar complexity is real; be disciplined about what ships in M1.\nRecommendation: in the new session, start with ADR-016 (the drawing-model decision itself) before anything else. Don't plan M1.3 until that ADR is landed. The rest cascades from it."}

If uncertain, ask.\n- If multiple interpretations exist, present them — don't pick silently.\n- If a simpler approach exists, say so. Push back when warranted.\n- If something is unclear, stop. Name what's confusing. Ask.\n\n## 2. Simplicity First\n\n**Minimum code that solves the problem. Nothing speculative.**\n\n- No features beyond what was asked.\n- No abstractions for single-use code.\n- No \"flexibility\" or \"configurability\" that wasn't requested.\n- No error handling for impossible scenarios.\n- If you write 200 lines and it could be 50, rewrite it.\n\nAsk yourself: \"Would a senior engineer say this is overcomplicated?\" If yes,\nsimplify.\n\n**Exception:** abstractions mandated by the project contract\n(`docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md`) are not discretionary,\neven when they look like overengineering for the current scope.\n\n## 3. Surgical Changes\n\n**Touch only what you must. Clean up only your own mess.**\n\nWhen editing existing code:\n- Don't \"improve\" adjacent code, comments, or formatting.\n- Don't refactor things that aren't broken.\n- Match existing style, even if you'd do it differently.\n- If you notice unrelated dead code, mention it — don't delete it.\n\nWhen your changes create orphans:\n- Remove imports/variables/functions that YOUR changes made unused.\n- Don't remove pre-existing dead code unless asked.\n\nThe test: Every changed line should trace directly to the user's request.\n\n## 4. Goal-Driven Execution\n\n**Define success criteria. Loop until verified.**\n\nTransform tasks into verifiable goals:\n- \"Add validation\" → \"Write tests for invalid inputs, then make them pass\"\n- \"Fix the bug\" → \"Write a test that reproduces it, then make it pass\"\n- \"Refactor X\" → \"Ensure tests pass before and after\"\n\nFor multi-step tasks, state a brief plan:\n\n```\n1. [Step] → verify: [check]\n2. [Step] → verify: [check]\n3. [Step] → verify: [check]\n```\n\nStrong success criteria let you loop independently. Weak criteria (\"make it\nwork\") require constant clarification.\n\n---\n\n## Project-Specific Routing\n\nBefore starting any substantive work in this repository, you MUST read the\napplicable procedure file from `docs/procedures/Claude/`. These are binding\noperating rules, not suggestions.\n\n| Procedure | Path | When to use |\n|-----------|------|-------------|\n| 00 — Architecture Contract | `docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md` | **Always read first.** Lists binding documents, ADR rules, registry rules, deviation protocol. |\n| 01 — Plan Authoring | `docs/procedures/Claude/01-plan-authoring.md` | Writing a new plan (PLAN-ONLY mode) |\n| 02 — Plan Review | `docs/procedures/Claude/02-plan-review.md` | Reviewing/scrutinising a plan before execution (READ-ONLY) |\n| 03 — Plan Execution | `docs/procedures/Claude/03-plan-execution.md` | Implementing an approved plan (AUDIT-FIRST mode) |\n| 04 — Post-Commit Review | `docs/procedures/Claude/04-post-commit-review.md` | Auditing committed code (READ-ONLY memo, no fixes) |\n| 05 — Post-Commit Remediation | `docs/procedures/Claude/05-post-commit-remediation.md` | Fixing issues found after commit |\n\n**Hard rules:**\n- MUST NOT skip reading the applicable procedure.\n- MUST NOT rely on memory of previous sessions. Procedure files are the\n  SSOT for operating rules. Re-read each session.\n- MUST NOT deviate from the architecture contract without following the\n  Approved Deviation Protocol in 00-architecture-contract.md.\n\n---\n\n**These guidelines are working if:** fewer unnecessary changes in diffs,\nfewer rewrites due to overcomplication, and clarifying questions come before\nimplementation rather than after mistakes.\n","numLines":103,"startLine":1,"totalLines":103}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"26c03619-5aab-4d10-98b7-33a2af36f951","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

Implementation that violates these is a\n22\t**Blocker** by default (see §0.7 Approved Deviation Protocol for the escape\n23\tvalve).\n24\t\n25\t### Architecture Decision Records\n26\t\n27\tAll files in `docs/adr/` are binding.\n28\t\n29\t| ID | Title | Path |\n30\t|----|-------|------|\n31\t| 001 | Coordinate System Strategy | `docs/adr/001-coordinate-system.md` |\n32\t| 002 | Object Model Contract | `docs/adr/002-object-model.md` |\n33\t| 003 | Ownership States | `docs/adr/003-ownership-states.md` |\n34\t| 004 | Parameter Extraction Contract | `docs/adr/004-parameter-extraction.md` |\n35\t| 005 | Library Model | `docs/adr/005-library-model.md` |\n36\t| 006 | Scenario Model | `docs/adr/006-scenario-model.md` |\n37\t| 007 | Validation Engine | `docs/adr/007-validation-engine.md` |\n38\t| 008 | 3D Derivation Cache | `docs/adr/008-3d-cache.md` |\n39\t| 009 | RBAC and Permissions | `docs/adr/009-rbac.md` |\n40\t| 010 | Project Sync and Offline | `docs/adr/010-project-sync.md` |\n41\t| 011 | UI Stack: Icon Library and Theme Switching | `docs/adr/011-ui-stack.md` |\n42\t| 012 | Technology Stack | `docs/adr/012-technology-stack.md` |\n43\t| 013 | 2D Rendering Pipeline | `docs/adr/013-2d-rendering-pipeline.md` |\n44\t| 014 | Persistence Architecture | `docs/adr/014-persistence-architecture.md` |\n45\t| 015 | Project Store and State Management Scope | `docs/adr/015-project-store-state-management.md` |\n46\t\n47\t**ADR rules:**\n48\t- ADRs MUST NOT be edited. If a decision changes, a new ADR MUST be written\n49\t  that references and supersedes the old one. The superseded ADR stays in\n50\t  the repository with `Status: SUPERSEDED` and a link to its replacement.\n51\t- Deviating from an ADR silently is a **Blocker**.\n52\t- Proposing a deviation requires the Approved Deviation Protocol (§0.7).\n53\t\n54\t### Parameter Extraction Registry\n55\t\n56\tAll entries in `docs/extraction-registry/` are binding specification written\n57\t**before** implementation.\n58\t\n59\t| Entry | Path |\n60\t|-------|------|\n61\t| Registry Governance | `docs/extraction-registry/README.md` |\n62\t| RTG_BLOCK | `docs/extraction-registry/RTG_BLOCK.md` |\n63\t| ROAD | `docs/extraction-registry/ROAD.md` |\n64\t| BUILDING | `docs/extraction-registry/BUILDING.md` |\n65\t| PAVEMENT_AREA | `docs/extraction-registry/PAVEMENT_AREA.md` |\n66\t| BERTH | `docs/extraction-registry/BERTH.md` |\n67\t| YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY | `docs/extraction-registry/YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md` |\n68\t| GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY | `docs/extraction-registry/GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md` |\n69\t\n70\t**Registry rules:**\n71\t- New object types, new extractors, new validation rules MUST be added to\n72\t  the registry **before** implementation.\n73\t- Changing an existing extractor formula MUST bump its semver version in\n74\t  the registry entry. Implementation without version bump is a **Blocker**.\n75\t- Adding a new object type without a registry entry is a **Blocker**.\n76\t- The extractor's `version` string in output bundles MUST match the\n77\t  registry entry version.\n78\t\n79\t### Domain specification\n80\t\n81\t| Doc | Path | Status |\n82\t|-----|------|--------|\n83\t| Domain Glossary | `docs/glossary.md` | Binding terminology |\n84\t| Coordinate System Reference | `docs/coordinate-system.md` | Binding |\n85\t| Design Tokens | `docs/design-tokens.md` | Binding for UI work |\n86\t\n87\t### Informative documents (not binding, but authoritative context)\n88\t\n89\t| Doc | Path |\n90\t|-----|------|\n91\t| System Overview | `docs/overview.md` |\n92\t| Execution Plan | `docs/execution-plan.md` |\n93\t| ADR Index | `docs/adr/README.md` |\n94\t\n95\t---\n96\t\n97\t## 0.3) Reference material (non-binding)\n98\t\n99\tThe `reference/` directory at repository root contains visual and\n100\tinteraction references only.\n101\t\n102\t- `reference/prototype-v1.html` — validated HTML prototype for visual\n103\t  design and UX validation.\n104\t- `reference/README.md` — explains what the prototype is and is not.\n105\t\n106\t**Rules:**\n107\t- MUST NOT port code patterns from `reference/`.\n108\t- MUST NOT treat the prototype's monolithic structure as a template.\n109\t- The prototype explicitly violates ADRs 001, 002, 004, 007, and 010.\n110\t- Use it only for visual design token validation and interaction pattern\n111\t  replication.\n112\t\n113\t---\n114\t\n115\t## 0.4) Ground Rules (applied across all procedures)\n116\t\n117\t### GR-1: PREPRODUCTION CLEAN-BREAK RULE\n118\t\n119\tThe application is preproduction. Backward compatibility is NOT required.\n120\t\n121\t- MUST NOT add migration shims, legacy adapters, deprecation bridges, or\n122\t  \"temporary compatibility\" code.\n123\t- If old architecture conflicts with target architecture, MUST replace old\n124\t  code directly.\n125\t\n126\t### GR-2: ARCHITECTURE-FIRST RULE\n127\t\n128\tNo shortcuts. No hacks. No \"good enough for now.\"\n129\t\n130\tEvery decision MUST be:\n131\t- SSOT-compliant (single source of truth per concept)\n132\t- DRY (no duplication of logic, formulas, or invariants)\n133\t- Scalable (supports the object types and scenarios beyond the current one)\n134\t- Explicitly testable (every invariant has a verification command or test)\n135\t- Operationally safe (undo/redo, hydration, serialization, document sync)\n136\t\n137\t### GR-3: MODULE ISOLATION AND CODE ORGANISATION\n138\t\n139\t**Module boundaries for this project:**\n140\t\n141\t```\n142\tpackages/domain/         Pure logic. Types, extractors, validators, generators.\n143\t                         MUST NOT depend on any other package.\n144\t                         MUST NOT import React, Zustand, or any stateful lib.\n145\t\n146\tpackages/project-store/      Project state (vanilla Zustand + zundo + Immer).\n147\t                         Depends on domain. MUST NOT import React.\n148\t                         MUST NOT own persistence (ADR-014 is authoritative).\n149\t\n150\tpackages/project-store-react/ React bindings for project-store (hooks, context).\n151\t                         Depends on project-store + domain. React as\n152\t                         peerDependency only (never a direct dependency —\n153\t                         see ADR-015).\n154\t\n155\tpackages/editor-2d/      2D canvas editor. Depends on domain + project-store\n156\t                         (and design-system for UI elements).\n157\t                         MAY depend on project-store-react inside React chrome\n158\t                         subdirectories (inspector panels, overlays).\n159\t                         Canvas paint loops MUST NOT import project-store-react.\n160\t                         MUST NOT depend on viewer-3d.\n161\t\n162\tpackages/viewer-3d/      3D derived viewer. Depends on domain + project-store\n163\t                         (and design-system).\n164\t                         MAY depend on project-store-react inside React chrome.\n165\t                         Scene rendering code MUST NOT import project-store-react.\n166\t                         MUST NOT depend on editor-2d.\n167\t\n168\tpackages/design-system/  Tokens and components.\n169\t                         MUST NOT depend on domain or any app.\n170\t\n171\tapps/web/                Integrates packages. Depends on all packages\n172\t                         including project-store-react for chrome hooks.\n173\t                         MUST NOT be imported from anywhere.\n174\t\n175\tservices/api/            Backend. Shares types from domain only.\n176\t                         MUST NOT import UI-specific code, project-store,\n177\t                         or project-store-react.\n178\t```\n179\t\n180\t**Isolation rules:**\n181\t- MUST NOT import from editor-2d into viewer-3d or vice versa.\n182\t- MUST NOT import from apps/web into any package.\n183\t- Cross-package imports are a **Blocker** unless they match the dependency\n184\t  graph above.\n185\t- Shared utilities that serve multiple packages MUST live in an\n186\t  appropriately owned package — never in a cross-cutting \"utils\" dump.\n187\t- **Canvas paint loops and 3D scene rendering MUST NOT import from\n188\t  `@portplanner/project-store-react`.** They import `@portplanner/project-store`\n189\t  directly and use `store.subscribe()` / `store.getState()`. This keeps\n190\t  React out of the rendering hot path.\n191\t\n192\t  Enforcement grep gate (applies when the subdirectories exist):\n193\t  ```\n194\t  rg -n \"from '@portplanner/project-store-react'\" \\\n195\t     packages/editor-2d/src/canvas/ \\\n196\t     packages/viewer-3d/src/scene/\n197\t  ```\n198\t  Expected: zero matches. Until those subdirectories exist, the gate\n199\t  passes trivially.\n200\t\n201\t**Folder structure and modularity:**\n202\t- Every folder MUST have a clear single owner (one domain concept, one\n203\t  feature, one utility concern).\n204\t- Files MUST be modular: one responsibility per file. If a file grows\n205\t  beyond ~400 LOC or mixes concerns, it MUST be split.\n206\t- Helpers serving a single component MUST live next to their consumer.\n207\t- MUST NOT create \"catch-all\" or \"misc\" files. Every file name MUST\n208\t  describe its contents.\n209\t- When creating a new file, MUST verify no existing file already covers\n210\t  that responsibility (DRY).\n211\t\n212\t---\n213\t\n214\t## 0.5) Spec update rule\n215\t\n216\tAny plan, execution, remediation, or review that changes behaviour\n217\tdescribed in a binding specification MUST update the relevant spec\n218\tdocument(s) **in the same commit** as the code change.\n219\t\n220\tSpecific examples:\n221\t- Adding a new extractor output field → update the registry entry and\n222\t  bump the version, in the same commit as the extractor code change.\n223\t- Changing an ownership state transition → either follow §0.7 Approved\n224\t  Deviation Protocol and write a new ADR, or reject the change.\n225\t- Adding a new design token → update `docs/design-tokens.md` in the\n226\t  same commit.\n227\t\n228\tFailure to update the relevant spec is a **Blocker**.\n229\t\n230\t---\n231\t\n232\t## 0.6) Architecture doc file lifecycle\n233\t\n234\t- ADR files: never edited after acceptance. Write a new ADR if the\n235\t  decision changes.\n236\t- Extraction registry entries: edited for version bumps and clarifications.\n237\t  Every change increments the version and adds a changelog line.\n238\t- Glossary: appended when new terms enter the codebase. Existing entries\n239\t  can be clarified but not redefined without an ADR.\n240\t- Design tokens: edited when the palette or scale evolves. Every change\n241\t  increments the document version in the changelog section.\n242\t\n243\t---\n244\t\n245\t## 0.7) Approved Deviation Protocol\n246\t\n247\t**Architecture specifications evolve.** ADRs were written before every\n248\tedge case was known. Extraction registry entries may prove insufficient\n249\tonce implementation exposes new requirements. Deviations from binding\n250\tspecifications are legitimate when the existing spec is wrong or\n251\tincomplete.\n252\t\n253\tHowever, **deviations are never silent.** Every deviation follows this\n254\tprotocol.\n255\t\n256\t### When a deviation is needed\n257\t\n258\tIf a plan, execution, or remediation needs to deviate from a binding\n259\tspecification, the implementer MUST:\n260\t\n261\t1. **Name the deviation explicitly** in the plan. Example: \"This plan\n262\t   proposes modifying ADR-003 ownership state transitions to add a new\n263\t   state: PENDING_REGENERATION, required by the generator to handle the\n264\t   race condition between regeneration triggers and user edits.\"\n265\t\n266\t2. **Justify the deviation** in a dedicated section of the plan:\n267\t   - What in the current specification does not work for this case\n268\t   - What was missed in the original specification\n269\t   - Why adapting the implementation without changing the spec is not\n270\t     sufficient\n271\t   - Why the new approach is correct\n272\t\n273\t3. **Propose the replacement**:\n274\t   - For an ADR: write a new superseding ADR that replaces the old one.\n275\t     The old ADR gets `Status: SUPERSEDED` and a link to the new one.\n276\t   - For an extraction registry entry: patch the entry and bump its\n277\t     version. If the change is major, consider a new entry.\n278\t   - For the glossary or design tokens: patch with a changelog line.\n279\t\n280\t4. **Flag the deviation in the pre-response notification** (see Procedure\n281\t   01 §1.12). The user MUST see deviations before the full plan.\n282\t\n283\t5. **Require explicit user approval.** The plan is NOT approved for\n284\t   execution until the user has explicitly acknowledged the deviation.\n285\t   Approval MUST be recorded in the plan file (date, user identifier,\n286\t   reason statement).\n287\t\n288\t6. **Commit the spec update alongside the implementation.** The new/updated\n289\t   ADR, registry entry, or doc change lands in the same PR as the code\n290\t   that depends on it. Never separate.\n291\t\n292\t### Classification\n293\t\n294\t- A deviation without user approval → **Blocker**.\n295\t- A deviation with approval but without the updated spec committed in the\n296\t  same PR → **Blocker**.\n297\t- A deviation with approval and updated spec committed together → legitimate\n298\t  evolution of the architecture.\n299\t\n300\t### What is NOT a deviation\n301\t\n302\t- Following an ADR literally but in a way the ADR did not explicitly\n303\t  enumerate. Example: ADR-002 does not list every possible object type,\n304\t  but adding `BERTH` as a new type conforming to the contract is not a\n305\t  deviation — it is expected extension.\n306\t- Adding a validation rule to an existing object type. The registry\n307\t  entry is updated, no ADR change needed.\n308\t- Refining an extraction formula to fix a bug. Bump the version, update\n309\t  the registry entry changelog, no ADR change.\n310\t\n311\t### What IS a deviation\n312\t\n313\t- Changing the semantics of an ownership state.\n314\t- Adding a new ownership state.\n315\t- Changing how the coordinate system works.\n316\t- Introducing a new data layer not covered by ADR-002.\n317\t- Changing the sync model from last-write-wins to CRDT-based.\n318\t- Any change that would make an existing ADR incorrect.\n319\t\n320\t### Progressive implementation (distinct from deviation)\n321\t\n322\tAn implementation that ships a **strict subset** of a binding\n323\tspecification at a given milestone is NOT classified as a deviation\n324\twhen ALL of the following conditions hold:\n325\t\n326\t1. **No conflicting runtime semantics.** The subset does not add\n327\t   fallback logic, warnings, proxies, or runtime behaviour absent\n328\t   from the spec.\n329\t2. **Excluded features unreachable at the type level.** Type\n330\t   narrowing MUST be additive-only so later widening (the full\n331\t   superset) does not break current-milestone consumers.\n332\t3. **User approval recorded in the plan file** with user identifier\n333\t   and date.\n334\t4. **Widening plan explicitly stated**: which milestone restores the\n335\t   full spec, named in the plan.\n336\t\n337\tIf any condition is not met, the change MUST follow the Approved\n338\tDeviation Protocol above as a deviation.\n339\t\n340\tProgressive implementation is the legitimate path when the execution\n341\tplan explicitly excludes a feature in the current milestone\n342\t(e.g. `docs/execution-plan.md` Milestone 1: \"pick dark or light, ship\n343\tone\"). Each plan applying this classification MUST include a mapping\n344\ttable demonstrating the four conditions hold, with references to the\n345\tplan sections that satisfy each.\n346\t\n347\t---\n348\t\n349\t## 0.8) Verification expectation\n350\t\n351\tEvery review (Procedures 02, 04) and every execution (Procedure 03) MUST\n352\tverify against this contract:\n353\t\n354\t- Binding specifications listed in §0.2 are consulted, not memorised.\n355\t- Any deviation found must trace to an approval per §0.7.\n356\t- Any missed spec update per §0.5 is flagged as a Blocker.\n357\t- Any GR-3 violation per §0.4 is flagged as a Blocker.\n358\t\n359\tIf you are unsure whether something is binding, treat it as binding and\n360\task.\n361\t"}]},"uuid":"c6cfe23d-5c91-4436-b30e-2bbd287be346","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:24.621Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\procedures\\Claude\\00-architecture-contract.md","content":"# Procedure 00 — Architecture Contract (Binding Specifications Reference)\n\n> **RFC 2119 convention**: \"MUST\", \"MUST NOT\", \"SHALL\", \"SHOULD\", and \"MAY\"\n> carry their standard meanings throughout this document.\n\n---\n\n## 0.1) Purpose\n\nThis document defines which specifications in the repository are **binding**\nand which are **informative**. If a decision changes, a new ADR MUST be written\n  that references and supersedes the old one. The superseded ADR stays in\n  the repository with `Status: SUPERSEDED` and a link to its replacement.\n- Deviating from an ADR silently is a **Blocker**.\n- Proposing a deviation requires the Approved Deviation Protocol (§0.7).\n\n### Parameter Extraction Registry\n\nAll entries in `docs/extraction-registry/` are binding specification written\n**before** implementation.\n\n| Entry | Path |\n|-------|------|\n| Registry Governance | `docs/extraction-registry/README.md` |\n| RTG_BLOCK | `docs/extraction-registry/RTG_BLOCK.md` |\n| ROAD | `docs/extraction-registry/ROAD.md` |\n| BUILDING | `docs/extraction-registry/BUILDING.md` |\n| PAVEMENT_AREA | `docs/extraction-registry/PAVEMENT_AREA.md` |\n| BERTH | `docs/extraction-registry/BERTH.md` |\n| YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY | `docs/extraction-registry/YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md` |\n| GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY | `docs/extraction-registry/GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md` |\n\n**Registry rules:**\n- New object types, new extractors, new validation rules MUST be added to\n  the registry **before** implementation.\n- Changing an existing extractor formula MUST bump its semver version in\n  the registry entry. Implementation without version bump is a **Blocker**.\n- Adding a new object type without a registry entry is a **Blocker**.\n- The extractor's `version` string in output bundles MUST match the\n  registry entry version.\n\n### Domain specification\n\n| Doc | Path | Status |\n|-----|------|--------|\n| Domain Glossary | `docs/glossary.md` | Binding terminology |\n| Coordinate System Reference | `docs/coordinate-system.md` | Binding |\n| Design Tokens | `docs/design-tokens.md` | Binding for UI work |\n\n### Informative documents (not binding, but authoritative context)\n\n| Doc | Path |\n|-----|------|\n| System Overview | `docs/overview.md` |\n| Execution Plan | `docs/execution-plan.md` |\n| ADR Index | `docs/adr/README.md` |\n\n---\n\n## 0.3) Reference material (non-binding)\n\nThe `reference/` directory at repository root contains visual and\ninteraction references only.\n\n- `reference/prototype-v1.html` — validated HTML prototype for visual\n  design and UX validation.\n- `reference/README.md` — explains what the prototype is and is not.\n\n**Rules:**\n- MUST NOT port code patterns from `reference/`.\n- MUST NOT treat the prototype's monolithic structure as a template.\n- The prototype explicitly violates ADRs 001, 002, 004, 007, and 010.\n- Use it only for visual design token validation and interaction pattern\n  replication.\n\n---\n\n## 0.4) Ground Rules (applied across all procedures)\n\n### GR-1: PREPRODUCTION CLEAN-BREAK RULE\n\nThe application is preproduction. Backward compatibility is NOT required.\n\n- MUST NOT add migration shims, legacy adapters, deprecation bridges, or\n  \"temporary compatibility\" code.\n- If old architecture conflicts with target architecture, MUST replace old\n  code directly.\n\n### GR-2: ARCHITECTURE-FIRST RULE\n\nNo shortcuts. No hacks. No \"good enough for now.\"\n\nEvery decision MUST be:\n- SSOT-compliant (single source of truth per concept)\n- DRY (no duplication of logic, formulas, or invariants)\n- Scalable (supports the object types and scenarios beyond the current one)\n- Explicitly testable (every invariant has a verification command or test)\n- Operationally safe (undo/redo, hydration, serialization, document sync)\n\n### GR-3: MODULE ISOLATION AND CODE ORGANISATION\n\n**Module boundaries for this project:**\n\n```\npackages/domain/         Pure logic. Types, extractors, validators, generators.\n                         MUST NOT depend on any other package.\n                         MUST NOT import React, Zustand, or any stateful lib.\n\npackages/project-store/      Project state (vanilla Zustand + zundo + Immer).\n                         Depends on domain. MUST NOT import React.\n                         MUST NOT own persistence (ADR-014 is authoritative).\n\npackages/project-store-react/ React bindings for project-store (hooks, context).\n                         Depends on project-store + domain. React as\n                         peerDependency only (never a direct dependency —\n                         see ADR-015).\n\npackages/editor-2d/      2D canvas editor. Depends on domain + project-store\n                         (and design-system for UI elements).\n                         MAY depend on project-store-react inside React chrome\n                         subdirectories (inspector panels, overlays).\n                         Canvas paint loops MUST NOT import project-store-react.\n                         MUST NOT depend on viewer-3d.\n\npackages/viewer-3d/      3D derived viewer. Depends on domain + project-store\n                         (and design-system).\n                         MAY depend on project-store-react inside React chrome.\n                         Scene rendering code MUST NOT import project-store-react.\n                         MUST NOT depend on editor-2d.\n\npackages/design-system/  Tokens and components.\n                         MUST NOT depend on domain or any app.\n\napps/web/                Integrates packages. Depends on all packages\n                         including project-store-react for chrome hooks.\n                         MUST NOT be imported from anywhere.\n\nservices/api/            Backend. Shares types from domain only.\n                         MUST NOT import UI-specific code, project-store,\n                         or project-store-react.\n```\n\n**Isolation rules:**\n- MUST NOT import from editor-2d into viewer-3d or vice versa.\n- MUST NOT import from apps/web into any package.\n- Cross-package imports are a **Blocker** unless they match the dependency\n  graph above.\n- Shared utilities that serve multiple packages MUST live in an\n  appropriately owned package — never in a cross-cutting \"utils\" dump.\n- **Canvas paint loops and 3D scene rendering MUST NOT import from\n  `@portplanner/project-store-react`.** They import `@portplanner/project-store`\n  directly and use `store.subscribe()` / `store.getState()`. This keeps\n  React out of the rendering hot path.\n\n  Enforcement grep gate (applies when the subdirectories exist):\n  ```\n  rg -n \"from '@portplanner/project-store-react'\" \\\n     packages/editor-2d/src/canvas/ \\\n     packages/viewer-3d/src/scene/\n  ```\n  Expected: zero matches. Until those subdirectories exist, the gate\n  passes trivially.\n\n**Folder structure and modularity:**\n- Every folder MUST have a clear single owner (one domain concept, one\n  feature, one utility concern).\n- Files MUST be modular: one responsibility per file. If a file grows\n  beyond ~400 LOC or mixes concerns, it MUST be split.\n- Helpers serving a single component MUST live next to their consumer.\n- MUST NOT create \"catch-all\" or \"misc\" files. Every file name MUST\n  describe its contents.\n- When creating a new file, MUST verify no existing file already covers\n  that responsibility (DRY).\n\n---\n\n## 0.5) Spec update rule\n\nAny plan, execution, remediation, or review that changes behaviour\ndescribed in a binding specification MUST update the relevant spec\ndocument(s) **in the same commit** as the code change.\n\nSpecific examples:\n- Adding a new extractor output field → update the registry entry and\n  bump the version, in the same commit as the extractor code change.\n- Changing an ownership state transition → either follow §0.7 Approved\n  Deviation Protocol and write a new ADR, or reject the change.\n- Adding a new design token → update `docs/design-tokens.md` in the\n  same commit.\n\nFailure to update the relevant spec is a **Blocker**.\n\n---\n\n## 0.6) Architecture doc file lifecycle\n\n- ADR files: never edited after acceptance. Write a new ADR if the\n  decision changes.\n- Extraction registry entries: edited for version bumps and clarifications.\n  Every change increments the version and adds a changelog line.\n- Glossary: appended when new terms enter the codebase. Existing entries\n  can be clarified but not redefined without an ADR.\n- Design tokens: edited when the palette or scale evolves. Every change\n  increments the document version in the changelog section.\n\n---\n\n## 0.7) Approved Deviation Protocol\n\n**Architecture specifications evolve.** ADRs were written before every\nedge case was known. Extraction registry entries may prove insufficient\nonce implementation exposes new requirements. Deviations from binding\nspecifications are legitimate when the existing spec is wrong or\nincomplete.\n\nHowever, **deviations are never silent.** Every deviation follows this\nprotocol.\n\n### When a deviation is needed\n\nIf a plan, execution, or remediation needs to deviate from a binding\nspecification, the implementer MUST:\n\n1. **Name the deviation explicitly** in the plan. Example: \"This plan\n   proposes modifying ADR-003 ownership state transitions to add a new\n   state: PENDING_REGENERATION, required by the generator to handle the\n   race condition between regeneration triggers and user edits.\"\n\n2. **Justify the deviation** in a dedicated section of the plan:\n   - What in the current specification does not work for this case\n   - What was missed in the original specification\n   - Why adapting the implementation without changing the spec is not\n     sufficient\n   - Why the new approach is correct\n\n3. **Propose the replacement**:\n   - For an ADR: write a new superseding ADR that replaces the old one.\n     The old ADR gets `Status: SUPERSEDED` and a link to the new one.\n   - For an extraction registry entry: patch the entry and bump its\n     version. If the change is major, consider a new entry.\n   - For the glossary or design tokens: patch with a changelog line.\n\n4. **Flag the deviation in the pre-response notification** (see Procedure\n   01 §1.12). The user MUST see deviations before the full plan.\n\n5. **Require explicit user approval.** The plan is NOT approved for\n   execution until the user has explicitly acknowledged the deviation.\n   Approval MUST be recorded in the plan file (date, user identifier,\n   reason statement).\n\n6. **Commit the spec update alongside the implementation.** The new/updated\n   ADR, registry entry, or doc change lands in the same PR as the code\n   that depends on it. Never separate.\n\n### Classification\n\n- A deviation without user approval → **Blocker**.\n- A deviation with approval but without the updated spec committed in the\n  same PR → **Blocker**.\n- A deviation with approval and updated spec committed together → legitimate\n  evolution of the architecture.\n\n### What is NOT a deviation\n\n- Following an ADR literally but in a way the ADR did not explicitly\n  enumerate. Example: ADR-002 does not list every possible object type,\n  but adding `BERTH` as a new type conforming to the contract is not a\n  deviation — it is expected extension.\n- Adding a validation rule to an existing object type. The registry\n  entry is updated, no ADR change needed.\n- Refining an extraction formula to fix a bug. Bump the version, update\n  the registry entry changelog, no ADR change.\n\n### What IS a deviation\n\n- Changing the semantics of an ownership state.\n- Adding a new ownership state.\n- Changing how the coordinate system works.\n- Introducing a new data layer not covered by ADR-002.\n- Changing the sync model from last-write-wins to CRDT-based.\n- Any change that would make an existing ADR incorrect.\n\n### Progressive implementation (distinct from deviation)\n\nAn implementation that ships a **strict subset** of a binding\nspecification at a given milestone is NOT classified as a deviation\nwhen ALL of the following conditions hold:\n\n1. **No conflicting runtime semantics.** The subset does not add\n   fallback logic, warnings, proxies, or runtime behaviour absent\n   from the spec.\n2. **Excluded features unreachable at the type level.** Type\n   narrowing MUST be additive-only so later widening (the full\n   superset) does not break current-milestone consumers.\n3. **User approval recorded in the plan file** with user identifier\n   and date.\n4. **Widening plan explicitly stated**: which milestone restores the\n   full spec, named in the plan.\n\nIf any condition is not met, the change MUST follow the Approved\nDeviation Protocol above as a deviation.\n\nProgressive implementation is the legitimate path when the execution\nplan explicitly excludes a feature in the current milestone\n(e.g. `docs/execution-plan.md` Milestone 1: \"pick dark or light, ship\none\"). Each plan applying this classification MUST include a mapping\ntable demonstrating the four conditions hold, with references to the\nplan sections that satisfy each.\n\n---\n\n## 0.8) Verification expectation\n\nEvery review (Procedures 02, 04) and every execution (Procedure 03) MUST\nverify against this contract:\n\n- Binding specifications listed in §0.2 are consulted, not memorised.\n- Any deviation found must trace to an approval per §0.7.\n- Any missed spec update per §0.5 is flagged as a Blocker.\n- Any GR-3 violation per §0.4 is flagged as a Blocker.\n\nIf you are unsure whether something is binding, treat it as binding and\nask.\n","numLines":361,"startLine":1,"totalLines":361}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b4f3ac98-085f-4e7c-914e-dbd87a93f8d5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"a9a6c95a-6b6e-4c62-8b23-98fa65923ecb","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01KhhBdP3h2oFrFrG27N9VXn","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR-002 — Object Model Contract\n2\t\n3\t**Status:** ACCEPTED\n4\t**Date:** 2026-04-16\n5\t\n6\t## Context\n7\t\n8\tEvery element in the system — road, building, RTG block, berth, pavement —\n9\tmust carry sufficient information for rendering, analysis, costing, 3D\n10\tprojection, and library traceability. These concerns have different audiences:\n11\ta drafter editing a road geometry, a cost engineer editing unit rates, a\n12\tlibrary manager maintaining global templates.\n13\t\n14\tIf all concerns are on the same flat object, a drafter can accidentally mutate\n15\tcommercial data. If they are fully separated into independent records, the\n16\tsystem becomes unnavigable and cross-concern queries become expensive.\n17\t\n18\t## Options considered\n19\t\n20\t**A. Single flat object with all fields.** Simple in one sense, but conflates\n21\tconcerns. Junior drafters can accidentally modify cost rates. Schema becomes\n22\tunwieldy as the product grows.\n23\t\n24\t**B. Separate tables per concern.** Clean separation. Joins become expensive\n25\tfor common queries. Schema drift across tables requires careful coordination.\n26\t\n27\t**C. Core object with typed extension records per concern.** Geometry and\n28\tclassification live on the object. Analysis bindings, cost bindings, and 3D\n29\trender metadata are separate records that reference the object by ID.\n30\t\n31\t## Decision\n32\t\n33\t**Option C.**\n34\t\n35\tThe core object shape:\n36\t\n37\t```typescript\n38\tinterface PortObject {\n39\t  // Identity — always first-class columns\n40\t  id: UUID;\n41\t  project_id: UUID;\n42\t  scenario_id: UUID | null;        // null = baseline\n43\t  type: ObjectType;                 // RTG_BLOCK, ROAD, BUILDING, etc.\n44\t  category: ObjectCategory;\n45\t  ownership: OwnershipState;        // AUTHORED | GENERATED | FROZEN | DETACHED\n46\t\n47\t  // Geometry — project-local metric\n48\t  geometry: GeoJSON;\n49\t  geometry_type: GeometryPrimitive;\n50\t\n51\t  // Classification\n52\t  classification: string;           // typed per object family\n53\t\n54\t  // Extensible parameters — JSONB\n55\t  parameters: ObjectParameters;     // physical and operational hints\n56\t\n57\t  // Traceability\n58\t  library_ref: UUID | null;\n59\t  library_version: string | null;\n60\t  generated_from: UUID | null;      // parent host_space_id if GENERATED\n61\t\n62\t  // Audit\n63\t  revision: number;\n64\t  created_by: UUID;\n65\t  updated_by: UUID;\n66\t  created_at: timestamp;\n67\t  updated_at: timestamp;\n68\t}\n69\t```\n70\t\n71\t**Discipline rule:** anything queried, filtered, sorted, joined, or enforced\n72\tagainst in business rules is a first-class column. Anything purely payload —\n73\textensible parameters, rendering hints, override bags — is JSONB. If\n74\t`object_type` or `project_id` ends up in JSONB, the discipline has failed.\n75\t\n76\tAnalysis bindings, cost bindings, and 3D render metadata are **separate\n77\trecords** keyed by `object_id`:\n78\t\n79\t```\n80\tobject_analysis_bindings (object_id, analysis_version, ...)\n81\tobject_cost_bindings    (object_id, cost_assembly_ref, ...)\n82\tobject_mesh_descriptors (object_id, geometry_fingerprint, ...)\n83\tobject_quantities       (object_id, scenario_id, extractor_version, bundle)\n84\t```\n85\t\n86\t## Consequences\n87\t\n88\t- Geometry editing cannot accidentally mutate commercial data.\n89\t- Cross-concern queries are explicit joins, auditable in code review.\n90\t- JSONB is constrained to genuinely extensible payload, not domain identity.\n91\t- Object type registry defines valid parameter shapes per type, enforced at\n92\t  the API boundary.\n93\t- Adding a new concern (e.g. environmental impact bindings) is additive — new\n94\t  table, no migration of existing objects.\n95\t\n96\t## What this makes harder\n97\t\n98\t- A full-fidelity object snapshot requires joining multiple tables. Common\n99\t  queries need a materialized view or an explicit hydration layer.\n100\t- Two-stage writes (object + its bindings) need transaction discipline.\n101\t- Simple object-level operations have a few more moving parts than a flat\n102\t  schema.\n103\t"}]},"uuid":"d6e5f337-ce7f-433b-a5db-6b5922d3fea6","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:28.614Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\002-object-model.md","content":"# ADR-002 — Object Model Contract\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-16\n\n## Context\n\nEvery element in the system — road, building, RTG block, berth, pavement —\nmust carry sufficient information for rendering, analysis, costing, 3D\nprojection, and library traceability. These concerns have different audiences:\na drafter editing a road geometry, a cost engineer editing unit rates, a\nlibrary manager maintaining global templates.\n\nIf all concerns are on the same flat object, a drafter can accidentally mutate\ncommercial data. If they are fully separated into independent records, the\nsystem becomes unnavigable and cross-concern queries become expensive.\n\n## Options considered\n\n**A. Single flat object with all fields.** Simple in one sense, but conflates\nconcerns. Junior drafters can accidentally modify cost rates. Schema becomes\nunwieldy as the product grows.\n\n**B. Separate tables per concern.** Clean separation. Joins become expensive\nfor common queries. Schema drift across tables requires careful coordination.\n\n**C. Core object with typed extension records per concern.** Geometry and\nclassification live on the object. Analysis bindings, cost bindings, and 3D\nrender metadata are separate records that reference the object by ID.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Option C.**\n\nThe core object shape:\n\n```typescript\ninterface PortObject {\n  // Identity — always first-class columns\n  id: UUID;\n  project_id: UUID;\n  scenario_id: UUID | null;        // null = baseline\n  type: ObjectType;                 // RTG_BLOCK, ROAD, BUILDING, etc.\n  category: ObjectCategory;\n  ownership: OwnershipState;        // AUTHORED | GENERATED | FROZEN | DETACHED\n\n  // Geometry — project-local metric\n  geometry: GeoJSON;\n  geometry_type: GeometryPrimitive;\n\n  // Classification\n  classification: string;           // typed per object family\n\n  // Extensible parameters — JSONB\n  parameters: ObjectParameters;     // physical and operational hints\n\n  // Traceability\n  library_ref: UUID | null;\n  library_version: string | null;\n  generated_from: UUID | null;      // parent host_space_id if GENERATED\n\n  // Audit\n  revision: number;\n  created_by: UUID;\n  updated_by: UUID;\n  created_at: timestamp;\n  updated_at: timestamp;\n}\n```\n\n**Discipline rule:** anything queried, filtered, sorted, joined, or enforced\nagainst in business rules is a first-class column. Anything purely payload —\nextensible parameters, rendering hints, override bags — is JSONB. If\n`object_type` or `project_id` ends up in JSONB, the discipline has failed.\n\nAnalysis bindings, cost bindings, and 3D render metadata are **separate\nrecords** keyed by `object_id`:\n\n```\nobject_analysis_bindings (object_id, analysis_version, ...)\nobject_cost_bindings    (object_id, cost_assembly_ref, ...)\nobject_mesh_descriptors (object_id, geometry_fingerprint, ...)\nobject_quantities       (object_id, scenario_id, extractor_version, bundle)\n```\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Geometry editing cannot accidentally mutate commercial data.\n- Cross-concern queries are explicit joins, auditable in code review.\n- JSONB is constrained to genuinely extensible payload, not domain identity.\n- Object type registry defines valid parameter shapes per type, enforced at\n  the API boundary.\n- Adding a new concern (e.g. environmental impact bindings) is additive — new\n  table, no migration of existing objects.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- A full-fidelity object snapshot requires joining multiple tables. Common\n  queries need a materialized view or an explicit hydration layer.\n- Two-stage writes (object + its bindings) need transaction discipline.\n- Simple object-level operations have a few more moving parts than a flat\n  schema.\n","numLines":103,"startLine":1,"totalLines":103}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a9a6c95a-6b6e-4c62-8b23-98fa65923ecb","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

A system that\n10\trequires continuous server connection to be useful will frustrate its users\n11\ton the very days they most need the tool.\n12\t\n13\tWhen connectivity returns, changes made offline must merge cleanly with\n14\tserver state and with any concurrent changes made by other team members.\n15\t\n16\t## Options considered\n17\t\n18\t**A. Server-dependent. All operations require online connection.** Simple.\n19\tFails the use case.\n20\t\n21\t**B. Full CRDT-based multi-user collaboration from day one (Yjs or\n22\tAutomerge).** Maximum capability. Large implementation investment.\n23\tDistorts the project model around synchronization complexity. Not justified\n24\tby V1 use cases (small teams, rarely simultaneous editing).\n25\t\n26\t**C. Single-writer offline with deterministic merge on reconnect. The\n27\tproject is a serializable value type. Changes are operations. Object-level\n28\tlast-write-wins on conflicts.** Supports offline. Handles low-contention\n29\tmulti-user. CRDT-compatible upgrade path for future.\n30\t\n31\t## Decision\n32\t\n33\t**Option C for V1. Option B design-compatible for V2.**\n34\t\n35\t### Project as serializable value\n36\t\n37\tThe project is a **serializable value type**. At any moment it is\n38\ta map `object_id → ObjectSnapshot`. Client maintains a local operation log since last sync.\n74\t2. Operations apply immediately to local project state.\n75\t3. On reconnect, client sends its operation log to the server.\n76\t4. Server applies operations in sequence, resolving conflicts at object level.\n77\t\n78\t### Conflict resolution\n79\t\n80\t**Object-level last-write-wins.**\n81\t\n82\t- If two users edited **different** objects: both changes apply, no conflict.\n83\t- If two users edited the **same** object: the later server-timestamped\n84\t  operation wins. The losing client receives a conflict notification showing\n85\t  both versions; user can choose to re-apply their change.\n86\t\n87\tThis is not full CRDT. It is not real-time simultaneous editing of the same\n88\tobject. It handles the primary V1 use case: one planner offline on site,\n89\tsyncing when back at the office; two colleagues working on different parts\n90\tof the same project.\n91\t\n92\t### Future CRDT compatibility\n93\t\n94\tThe operation log structure is compatible with CRDT adoption. CRDTs refine\n95\thow conflicts resolve; the operation log model persists. Migrating to a\n96\tCRDT-based model in V2 is an upgrade of the merge resolution layer, not a\n97\trewrite of the project model.\n98\t\n99\t## Consequences\n100\t\n101\t- Full offline capability for single-user workflows.\n102\t- Clean sync for low-contention multi-user workflows.\n103\t- Explicit conflict notification for high-contention cases — user knows\n104\t  when their change was overwritten.\n105\t- The project remains a serializable value type: testable, snapshotable,\n106\t  migratable.\n107\t- Undo/redo is a natural consequence of the operation log (reverse the\n108\t  last N operations).\n109\t- V2 multi-user real-time editing is an additive upgrade.\n110\t\n111\t## What this makes harder\n112\t\n113\t- Client must maintain a local operation log with durable storage\n114\t  (IndexedDB).\n115\t- Sync protocol must handle partial failures (server accepts some\n116\t  operations, rejects others).\n117\t- Timestamp skew between clients must be handled (server timestamps are\n118\t  authoritative for ordering on conflict).\n119\t- Undo across a sync boundary (did we sync a mistake?) needs a\n120\t  clearly-communicated UI: user can undo locally, which generates new\n121\t  operations that reverse earlier ones, rather than trying to literally\n122\t  reverse time on the server.\n123\t\n124\t## Naming note (2026-04-22)\n125\t\n126\tEarlier drafts of this ADR used \"document\" / \"project document\" as the\n127\tterm for the serializable value type. That term has been retired in favour\n128\tof \"project\" — the simpler, user-facing word. Semantics are unchanged; the\n129\tvocabulary is consistent with the glossary's \"Project\" entry.\n130\t"}]},"uuid":"2cbeabd3-56fa-4f40-8331-2430d986bbd2","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:29.075Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\010-project-sync.md","content":"# ADR-010 — Project Sync and Offline Model\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-16\n\n## Context\n\nPort planners work on site, on vessels during inspection, in remote project\nlocations, and in client offices with variable connectivity. A system that\nrequires continuous server connection to be useful will frustrate its users\non the very days they most need the tool.\n\nWhen connectivity returns, changes made offline must merge cleanly with\nserver state and with any concurrent changes made by other team members.\n\n## Options considered\n\n**A. Server-dependent. All operations require online connection.** Simple.\nFails the use case.\n\n**B. Full CRDT-based multi-user collaboration from day one (Yjs or\nAutomerge).** Maximum capability. Large implementation investment.\nDistorts the project model around synchronization complexity. Not justified\nby V1 use cases (small teams, rarely simultaneous editing).\n\n**C. Single-writer offline with deterministic merge on reconnect. The\nproject is a serializable value type. Changes are operations. Object-level\nlast-write-wins on conflicts.** Supports offline. Handles low-contention\nmulti-user. CRDT-compatible upgrade path for future.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Option C for V1. Option B design-compatible for V2.**\n\n### Project as serializable value\n\nThe project is a **serializable value type**. At any moment it is\na map `object_id → ObjectSnapshot`. Every mutation produces a new valid\nproject state. The project is never mutated in place at the architectural\nlevel (implementation may use in-place mutation for performance; what\nmatters is that externally it behaves as immutable).\n\n### Operations\n\nEvery mutation is an **operation** logged with:\n\n```typescript\ninterface Operation {\n  id: UUID;\n  project_id: UUID;\n  sequence: number;                    // local monotonic counter per client\n  timestamp: timestamp;\n  user_id: UUID;\n  type: OperationType;                 // CREATE | UPDATE | DELETE | GENERATE | FREEZE\n  object_id: UUID;\n  before: ObjectSnapshot | null;       // pre-operation state (for undo)\n  after: ObjectSnapshot | null;        // post-operation state\n}\n\nenum OperationType {\n  CREATE,\n  UPDATE,\n  DELETE,\n  GENERATE,      // batch from generator\n  FREEZE,        // ownership state transition\n  DETACH,\n  UNFREEZE\n}\n```\n\n### Offline behaviour\n\n1. Client maintains a local operation log since last sync.\n2. Operations apply immediately to local project state.\n3. On reconnect, client sends its operation log to the server.\n4. Server applies operations in sequence, resolving conflicts at object level.\n\n### Conflict resolution\n\n**Object-level last-write-wins.**\n\n- If two users edited **different** objects: both changes apply, no conflict.\n- If two users edited the **same** object: the later server-timestamped\n  operation wins. The losing client receives a conflict notification showing\n  both versions; user can choose to re-apply their change.\n\nThis is not full CRDT. It is not real-time simultaneous editing of the same\nobject. It handles the primary V1 use case: one planner offline on site,\nsyncing when back at the office; two colleagues working on different parts\nof the same project.\n\n### Future CRDT compatibility\n\nThe operation log structure is compatible with CRDT adoption. CRDTs refine\nhow conflicts resolve; the operation log model persists. Migrating to a\nCRDT-based model in V2 is an upgrade of the merge resolution layer, not a\nrewrite of the project model.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Full offline capability for single-user workflows.\n- Clean sync for low-contention multi-user workflows.\n- Explicit conflict notification for high-contention cases — user knows\n  when their change was overwritten.\n- The project remains a serializable value type: testable, snapshotable,\n  migratable.\n- Undo/redo is a natural consequence of the operation log (reverse the\n  last N operations).\n- V2 multi-user real-time editing is an additive upgrade.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- Client must maintain a local operation log with durable storage\n  (IndexedDB).\n- Sync protocol must handle partial failures (server accepts some\n  operations, rejects others).\n- Timestamp skew between clients must be handled (server timestamps are\n  authoritative for ordering on conflict).\n- Undo across a sync boundary (did we sync a mistake?) needs a\n  clearly-communicated UI: user can undo locally, which generates new\n  operations that reverse earlier ones, rather than trying to literally\n  reverse time on the server.\n\n## Naming note (2026-04-22)\n\nEarlier drafts of this ADR used \"document\" / \"project document\" as the\nterm for the serializable value type. That term has been retired in favour\nof \"project\" — the simpler, user-facing word. Semantics are unchanged; the\nvocabulary is consistent with the glossary's \"Project\" entry.\n","numLines":130,"startLine":1,"totalLines":130}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"d30222f1-034f-4ada-94da-559bddf7b0a5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}
