{"parentUuid":"f20aacff-91f2-4820-88da-22c03aeb790c","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_011jGHjnwV914L7iCgqSdjKL","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR-013 — 2D Rendering Pipeline\n2\t\n3\t**Status:** ACCEPTED\n4\t**Date:** 2026-04-18\n5\t\n6\t## Context\n7\t\n8\tThe `packages/editor-2d` package is the primary surface area in Milestones 1\n9\tand 2. It must:\n10\t\n11\t- Render the authoritative 2D project (ADR-001 project-local metric\n12\t  geometry, ADR-002 typed objects).\n13\t- Support interactive authoring (draw, select, move, rotate, reshape).\n14\t- Support CAD-style interactions: object snap (OSNAP) to endpoints,\n15\t  midpoints, intersections, centers; polar tracking; ortho mode; object-snap\n16\t  tracking (OTRACK); dynamic dimension lines.\n17\t- Render overlays (snap markers, alignment guides, dimension text, selection\n18\t  handles) during interaction.\n19\t- Scale to Milestone 3 generated RTG blocks — potentially 10k+ container-level\n20\t  shapes per project.\n21\t- Honor the theme system (`useActiveThemeTokens()` bridge per ADR-011).\n22\t- Work within the op-log-driven project model (ADR-010) without introducing\n23\t  a parallel source of truth for object state.\n24\t\n25\tChoosing the wrong rendering foundation is expensive to undo. Once components\n26\tand interactions are built on top, migrating to a different renderer touches\n27\tevery consumer. This ADR pins the choice before implementation starts.\n28\t\n29\t## Options considered\n30\t\n31\t### Renderer\n32\t\n33\t**A. SVG (retained-mode DOM).** Each shape is a DOM node with CSS selectors\n34\tand native hit testing.\n35\t\n36\t- Pros: resolution-independent; free hit testing via `element.matches`;\n37\t  accessible; easy PNG/SVG export.\n38\t- Cons: DOM node-per-shape does not scale past ~1–5k elements; panning\n39\t  triggers layout; even hidden nodes cost reflow; sub-pixel artifacts at\n40\t  extreme zoom from viewport transform precision.\n41\t\n42\t**B. Plain Canvas2D (immediate mode).** Imperative `ctx.moveTo` / `ctx.lineTo`\n43\t/ `ctx.stroke` each frame. No retained scene. Redraw on every zoom/pan.\n44\t\n45\t- Pros: scales to 50k+ shapes; level-of-detail trivial (conditional inside\n46\t  paint function); frustum culling free; devicePixelRatio handling is ~10 LOC.\n47\t- Cons: hit testing requires custom geometry math; text rendering slightly\n48\t  less rich than SVG + CSS; no DOM to inspect.\n49\t\n50\t**C. Canvas2D with a scene-graph wrapper (Konva, Paper.js).** Library maintains\n51\tits own object tree; attaches event handlers per shape.\n52\t\n53\t- Pros: saves ~500–2000 LOC of hit-test boilerplate; layer-based caching.\n54\t- Cons: the scene graph is a **second source of truth** that must mirror the\n55\t  op-log document (ADR-010). Every create/update/delete mutates two\n56\t  structures; undo/redo must tear down and rebuild scene nodes in sync.\n57\t  Duplicates the invalidation pattern of ADR-008.\n58\t\n59\t**D. WebGL (Pixi.js or raw).** GPU rasterization with shaders.\n60\t\n61\t- Pros: scales to 100k+ shapes; shader effects.\n62\t- Cons: overkill for M1; shader debugging cost; text rendering painful;\n63\t  harder to hire for.\n64\t\n65\t### Zoom behaviour (common misconception)\n66\t\n67\tCanvas2D is not pixelated at zoom when used correctly. The draw loop\n68\tre-runs on every zoom change, passing the new transform matrix to the\n69\tcontext. `ctx.lineTo(x, y)` accepts floating-point screen coordinates — at\n70\t5× zoom you pass 5× larger values and the browser rasterizes a fresh vector\n71\tpath at full pixel precision. Identical crispness to SVG at every zoom level.\n72\tFigma, AutoCAD Web, Miro, FigJam, tldraw, and the post-migration Excalidraw\n73\tall use Canvas (or Canvas + WebGL). Authoritative geometry stays in\n74\tproject-local metres as Float64 (ADR-001); rasterization happens once per\n75\tframe at the final zoom.\n76\t\n77\t### Geometry math library\n78\t\n79\t**A. `@flatten-js/core`.** Typed 2D Euclidean primitives (Point, Segment,\n80\tLine, Circle, Polygon); intersections, distances, projections, boolean ops.\n81\t\n82\t- Pros: exactly the primitives OSNAP / OTRACK / polar need; typed; small;\n83\t  actively maintained.\n84\t- Cons: one more dependency.\n85\t\n86\t**B. Roll our own.** Write primitives as needed.\n87\t\n88\t- Pros: zero deps; full control.\n89\t- Cons: ~500 LOC of geometry primitives; subtle bugs in segment-segment\n90\t  intersection are easy to introduce.\n91\t\n92\t**C. `turf.js`.** GeoJSON-first geospatial operations.\n93\t\n94\t- Cons: heavy; geospatial-first; we work in project-local metric per ADR-001.\n95\t\n96\t**D. `martinez-polygon-clipping` + ad-hoc.** Polygon boolean ops only.\n97\t\n98\t- Cons: does not cover intersection / projection primitives.\n99\t\n100\t### Spatial index\n101\t\n102\t**A. `rbush` (R-tree).** Dynamic R-tree index; nearest-neighbor and\n103\tbounding-box queries.\n104\t\n105\t- Pros: mature; small; exactly the interface CAD snap needs.\n106\t- Cons: one dependency.\n107\t\n108\t**B. `kdbush` (k-d tree, point-only).** Cons: points only.\n109\t\n110\t**C. `flatbush`.** Cons: static-only — full rebuild on each mutation; wrong\n111\tfor interactive editing.\n112\t\n113\t**D. Roll our own (grid or naive scan).** Cons: naive scan is O(n) per\n114\tquery; grid index degrades for clustered layouts typical of port drawings.\n115\t\n116\t### View-transform layer\n117\t\n118\t**A. Roll our own (~100 LOC).** Linear domain→range mapping; mouse-wheel\n119\tzoom; click-drag pan; keyboard shortcuts.\n120\t\n121\t- Pros: full control over snap-aware zoom and CAD keyboard ergonomics.\n122\t- Cons: ~100 LOC to write.\n123\t\n124\t**B. `d3-zoom`.** Generic zoom/pan behavior.\n125\t\n126\t- Pros: battle-tested.\n127\t- Cons: designed for data-visualization patterns; customising for\n128\t  snap-aware zoom and keyboard shortcuts needs override scaffolding; ~5 KB\n129\t  we can save.\n130\t\n131\t## Decision\n132\t\n133\t| Aspect | Choice |\n134\t|---|---|\n135\t| Renderer | **Plain Canvas2D**, imperative `paint(ctx, state)` pattern, driven by the op-log-backed project state (ADR-010). `devicePixelRatio` handled at canvas init. |\n136\t| Geometry math | **`@flatten-js/core`** for 2D Euclidean primitives. Revisit only if it becomes a measured bottleneck or a better-typed alternative emerges. |\n137\t| Spatial index | **`rbush`** (R-tree) over object bounding boxes for hit testing, snap targeting, and frustum culling. |\n138\t| View transform | **Roll our own** view-transform layer (~100 LOC). No `d3-zoom` dependency. |\n139\t\n140\t### The paint pattern\n141\t\n142\t```\n143\tpaint(ctx, documentState, viewState, overlayState):\n144\t  clear(ctx)\n145\t  applyViewTransform(ctx, viewState)           // pan + zoom + DPR\n146\t  visible = rbush.search(viewFrustum)\n147\t  for each object in visible:\n148\t    drawObject(ctx, object, theme)\n149\t  drawOverlays(ctx, overlayState, theme)       // snap markers, guides, dimensions\n150\t```\n151\t\n152\t- `projectState` is a Zustand selector on the project store (ADR-012).\n153\t- `viewState` is a separate slice (zoom, pan). Not undoable.\n154\t- `overlayState` is ephemeral UI state (active snap target, alignment lines,\n155\t  dimension preview). Not undoable.\n156\t- Redraw is triggered by Zustand `store.subscribe` on the relevant slices\n157\t  and by explicit `invalidate()` calls during interaction.\n158\t\n159\t### Why not Konva / Paper / Pixi / SVG / WebGL\n160\t\n161\t- **SVG:** DOM-cost ceiling at Milestone 3 scale; pan thrashes layout.\n162\t- **Konva, Paper.js:** second scene graph duplicates the op-log document\n163\t  (ADR-010); adds synchronization surface for every mutation.\n164\t- **Pixi.js, raw WebGL:** overkill for M1; shader debugging cost; text\n165\t  rendering pain.\n166\t- **Static export** (PNG, SVG) for reports and prints is handled separately\n167\t  via a dedicated render-to-export path when that feature lands (post-M1).\n168\t\n169\t### What this ADR does NOT decide\n170\t\n171\tThe following are execution-phase design choices that emerge during M1\n172\timplementation, not pre-decided here:\n173\t\n174\t- Tool state machine (SELECT, LINE, POLYGON, RTG_BLOCK).\n175\t- Snap engine implementation: priority resolution between overlapping\n176\t  candidates, tolerance thresholds, visual hierarchy of snap markers.\n177\t- Command / operation dispatch (already constrained by ADR-010; details in\n178\t  execution).\n179\t- Selection model (single vs multi; rubber-band semantics).\n180\t- Fillet and other node-level interactions.\n181\t\n182\tIf any of these reveal a shortcoming in this ADR during execution, the\n183\tremedy is a superseding ADR via §0.7, not silent drift.\n184\t\n185\t## Consequences\n186\t\n187\t- The 2D editor scales to Milestone 3 generated-content volumes without\n188\t  architectural rework.\n189\t- Level-of-detail, frustum culling, and interactive overlays are first-class\n190\t  in the paint loop.\n191\t- OSNAP / OTRACK / polar / ortho / dynamic dimensions are implementable as\n192\t  pure geometry + overlay draw code; no renderer-specific wrappers.\n193\t- Theme swaps trigger canvas redraw via the `useActiveThemeTokens()`\n194\t  dependency from ADR-011.\n195\t- `rbush` + `@flatten-js/core` form the editor's computation core; both are\n196\t  testable independently of rendering.\n197\t\n198\t## What this makes harder\n199\t\n200\t- Hit testing is our responsibility. An R-tree bounding-box query followed\n201\t  by a per-candidate geometry check is the standard pattern; no\n202\t  `element.matches` fallback.\n203\t- Text rendering quirks (font metrics, baseline positioning) must be handled\n204\t  explicitly when drawing labels and dimensions.\n205\t- Debugging a draw bug requires stepping through paint code; there is no\n206\t  \"inspect element\" equivalent on the canvas.\n207\t- Static image export (PNG, SVG) requires a separate render path when that\n208\t  feature lands.\n209\t\n210\t## Cross-references\n211\t\n212\t- **ADR-001** Coordinate System — geometry is project-local metric; view\n213\t  transform converts to screen pixels at render time.\n214\t- **ADR-002** Object Model — object geometry stored in GeoJSON with\n215\t  project-local coordinates; paint code reads the core object record.\n216\t- **ADR-008** 3D Derivation Cache — uses fingerprint-keyed descriptors; 2D\n217\t  rendering follows the same philosophy (derive from authoritative state;\n218\t  don't retain a parallel scene).\n219\t- **ADR-010** Project Sync — the project is the single source of truth;\n220\t  paint reads a selector, never mutates.\n221\t- **ADR-011** UI Stack — `ThemeProvider` and `useActiveThemeTokens()` feed\n222\t  canvas draw state.\n223\t- **ADR-012** Technology Stack — Zustand for state subscriptions; Biome for\n224\t  lint; pinned Node, pnpm, Vite versions.\n225\t\n226\t## Changelog\n227\t\n228\t| Version | Date | Change |\n229\t|---|---|---|\n230\t| 1.0.0 | 2026-04-18 | Initial ADR. Pins M1 2D rendering foundations. |\n231\t"}]},"uuid":"ac322083-1bfc-444f-8244-775f234649fd","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:29.404Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\013-2d-rendering-pipeline.md","content":"# ADR-013 — 2D Rendering Pipeline\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-18\n\n## Context\n\nThe `packages/editor-2d` package is the primary surface area in Milestones 1\nand 2. It must:\n\n- Render the authoritative 2D project (ADR-001 project-local metric\n  geometry, ADR-002 typed objects).\n- Support interactive authoring (draw, select, move, rotate, reshape).\n- Support CAD-style interactions: object snap (OSNAP) to endpoints,\n  midpoints, intersections, centers; polar tracking; ortho mode; object-snap\n  tracking (OTRACK); dynamic dimension lines.\n- Render overlays (snap markers, alignment guides, dimension text, selection\n  handles) during interaction.\n- Scale to Milestone 3 generated RTG blocks — potentially 10k+ container-level\n  shapes per project.\n- Honor the theme system (`useActiveThemeTokens()` bridge per ADR-011).\n- Work within the op-log-driven project model (ADR-010) without introducing\n  a parallel source of truth for object state.\n\nChoosing the wrong rendering foundation is expensive to undo. Once components\nand interactions are built on top, migrating to a different renderer touches\nevery consumer. This ADR pins the choice before implementation starts.\n\n## Options considered\n\n### Renderer\n\n**A. SVG (retained-mode DOM).** Each shape is a DOM node with CSS selectors\nand native hit testing.\n\n- Pros: resolution-independent; free hit testing via `element.matches`;\n  accessible; easy PNG/SVG export.\n- Cons: DOM node-per-shape does not scale past ~1–5k elements; panning\n  triggers layout; even hidden nodes cost reflow; sub-pixel artifacts at\n  extreme zoom from viewport transform precision.\n\n**B. Plain Canvas2D (immediate mode).** Imperative `ctx.moveTo` / `ctx.lineTo`\n/ `ctx.stroke` each frame. No retained scene. Redraw on every zoom/pan.\n\n- Pros: scales to 50k+ shapes; level-of-detail trivial (conditional inside\n  paint function); frustum culling free; devicePixelRatio handling is ~10 LOC.\n- Cons: hit testing requires custom geometry math; text rendering slightly\n  less rich than SVG + CSS; no DOM to inspect.\n\n**C. Canvas2D with a scene-graph wrapper (Konva, Paper.js).** Library maintains\nits own object tree; attaches event handlers per shape.\n\n- Pros: saves ~500–2000 LOC of hit-test boilerplate; layer-based caching.\n- Cons: the scene graph is a **second source of truth** that must mirror the\n  op-log document (ADR-010). Every create/update/delete mutates two\n  structures; undo/redo must tear down and rebuild scene nodes in sync.\n  Duplicates the invalidation pattern of ADR-008.\n\n**D. WebGL (Pixi.js or raw).** GPU rasterization with shaders.\n\n- Pros: scales to 100k+ shapes; shader effects.\n- Cons: overkill for M1; shader debugging cost; text rendering painful;\n  harder to hire for.\n\n### Zoom behaviour (common misconception)\n\nCanvas2D is not pixelated at zoom when used correctly. The draw loop\nre-runs on every zoom change, passing the new transform matrix to the\ncontext. `ctx.lineTo(x, y)` accepts floating-point screen coordinates — at\n5× zoom you pass 5× larger values and the browser rasterizes a fresh vector\npath at full pixel precision. Identical crispness to SVG at every zoom level.\nFigma, AutoCAD Web, Miro, FigJam, tldraw, and the post-migration Excalidraw\nall use Canvas (or Canvas + WebGL). Authoritative geometry stays in\nproject-local metres as Float64 (ADR-001); rasterization happens once per\nframe at the final zoom.\n\n### Geometry math library\n\n**A. `@flatten-js/core`.** Typed 2D Euclidean primitives (Point, Segment,\nLine, Circle, Polygon); intersections, distances, projections, boolean ops.\n\n- Pros: exactly the primitives OSNAP / OTRACK / polar need; typed; small;\n  actively maintained.\n- Cons: one more dependency.\n\n**B. Roll our own.** Write primitives as needed.\n\n- Pros: zero deps; full control.\n- Cons: ~500 LOC of geometry primitives; subtle bugs in segment-segment\n  intersection are easy to introduce.\n\n**C. `turf.js`.** GeoJSON-first geospatial operations.\n\n- Cons: heavy; geospatial-first; we work in project-local metric per ADR-001.\n\n**D. `martinez-polygon-clipping` + ad-hoc.** Polygon boolean ops only.\n\n- Cons: does not cover intersection / projection primitives.\n\n### Spatial index\n\n**A. `rbush` (R-tree).** Dynamic R-tree index; nearest-neighbor and\nbounding-box queries.\n\n- Pros: mature; small; exactly the interface CAD snap needs.\n- Cons: one dependency.\n\n**B. `kdbush` (k-d tree, point-only).** Cons: points only.\n\n**C. `flatbush`.** Cons: static-only — full rebuild on each mutation; wrong\nfor interactive editing.\n\n**D. Roll our own (grid or naive scan).** Cons: naive scan is O(n) per\nquery; grid index degrades for clustered layouts typical of port drawings.\n\n### View-transform layer\n\n**A. Roll our own (~100 LOC).** Linear domain→range mapping; mouse-wheel\nzoom; click-drag pan; keyboard shortcuts.\n\n- Pros: full control over snap-aware zoom and CAD keyboard ergonomics.\n- Cons: ~100 LOC to write.\n\n**B. `d3-zoom`.** Generic zoom/pan behavior.\n\n- Pros: battle-tested.\n- Cons: designed for data-visualization patterns; customising for\n  snap-aware zoom and keyboard shortcuts needs override scaffolding; ~5 KB\n  we can save.\n\n## Decision\n\n| Aspect | Choice |\n|---|---|\n| Renderer | **Plain Canvas2D**, imperative `paint(ctx, state)` pattern, driven by the op-log-backed project state (ADR-010). `devicePixelRatio` handled at canvas init. |\n| Geometry math | **`@flatten-js/core`** for 2D Euclidean primitives. Revisit only if it becomes a measured bottleneck or a better-typed alternative emerges. |\n| Spatial index | **`rbush`** (R-tree) over object bounding boxes for hit testing, snap targeting, and frustum culling. |\n| View transform | **Roll our own** view-transform layer (~100 LOC). No `d3-zoom` dependency. |\n\n### The paint pattern\n\n```\npaint(ctx, documentState, viewState, overlayState):\n  clear(ctx)\n  applyViewTransform(ctx, viewState)           // pan + zoom + DPR\n  visible = rbush.search(viewFrustum)\n  for each object in visible:\n    drawObject(ctx, object, theme)\n  drawOverlays(ctx, overlayState, theme)       // snap markers, guides, dimensions\n```\n\n- `projectState` is a Zustand selector on the project store (ADR-012).\n- `viewState` is a separate slice (zoom, pan). Not undoable.\n- `overlayState` is ephemeral UI state (active snap target, alignment lines,\n  dimension preview). Not undoable.\n- Redraw is triggered by Zustand `store.subscribe` on the relevant slices\n  and by explicit `invalidate()` calls during interaction.\n\n### Why not Konva / Paper / Pixi / SVG / WebGL\n\n- **SVG:** DOM-cost ceiling at Milestone 3 scale; pan thrashes layout.\n- **Konva, Paper.js:** second scene graph duplicates the op-log document\n  (ADR-010); adds synchronization surface for every mutation.\n- **Pixi.js, raw WebGL:** overkill for M1; shader debugging cost; text\n  rendering pain.\n- **Static export** (PNG, SVG) for reports and prints is handled separately\n  via a dedicated render-to-export path when that feature lands (post-M1).\n\n### What this ADR does NOT decide\n\nThe following are execution-phase design choices that emerge during M1\nimplementation, not pre-decided here:\n\n- Tool state machine (SELECT, LINE, POLYGON, RTG_BLOCK).\n- Snap engine implementation: priority resolution between overlapping\n  candidates, tolerance thresholds, visual hierarchy of snap markers.\n- Command / operation dispatch (already constrained by ADR-010; details in\n  execution).\n- Selection model (single vs multi; rubber-band semantics).\n- Fillet and other node-level interactions.\n\nIf any of these reveal a shortcoming in this ADR during execution, the\nremedy is a superseding ADR via §0.7, not silent drift.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- The 2D editor scales to Milestone 3 generated-content volumes without\n  architectural rework.\n- Level-of-detail, frustum culling, and interactive overlays are first-class\n  in the paint loop.\n- OSNAP / OTRACK / polar / ortho / dynamic dimensions are implementable as\n  pure geometry + overlay draw code; no renderer-specific wrappers.\n- Theme swaps trigger canvas redraw via the `useActiveThemeTokens()`\n  dependency from ADR-011.\n- `rbush` + `@flatten-js/core` form the editor's computation core; both are\n  testable independently of rendering.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- Hit testing is our responsibility. An R-tree bounding-box query followed\n  by a per-candidate geometry check is the standard pattern; no\n  `element.matches` fallback.\n- Text rendering quirks (font metrics, baseline positioning) must be handled\n  explicitly when drawing labels and dimensions.\n- Debugging a draw bug requires stepping through paint code; there is no\n  \"inspect element\" equivalent on the canvas.\n- Static image export (PNG, SVG) requires a separate render path when that\n  feature lands.\n\n## Cross-references\n\n- **ADR-001** Coordinate System — geometry is project-local metric; view\n  transform converts to screen pixels at render time.\n- **ADR-002** Object Model — object geometry stored in GeoJSON with\n  project-local coordinates; paint code reads the core object record.\n- **ADR-008** 3D Derivation Cache — uses fingerprint-keyed descriptors; 2D\n  rendering follows the same philosophy (derive from authoritative state;\n  don't retain a parallel scene).\n- **ADR-010** Project Sync — the project is the single source of truth;\n  paint reads a selector, never mutates.\n- **ADR-011** UI Stack — `ThemeProvider` and `useActiveThemeTokens()` feed\n  canvas draw state.\n- **ADR-012** Technology Stack — Zustand for state subscriptions; Biome for\n  lint; pinned Node, pnpm, Vite versions.\n\n## Changelog\n\n| Version | Date | Change |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1.0.0 | 2026-04-18 | Initial ADR. Pins M1 2D rendering foundations. |\n","numLines":231,"startLine":1,"totalLines":231}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f20aacff-91f2-4820-88da-22c03aeb790c","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"f2481beb-86f7-4f21-a61b-28b12fb2ac2c","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01KFY99YPCnXGZRbscXosB7z","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Execution Plan\n2\t\n3\t## Principle\n4\t\n5\tShip a closed loop end-to-end before widening the feature set. The architecture\n6\tis good enough. The risk now is analysis paralysis dressed as rigour.\n7\t\n8\t## Milestone 1 — The end-to-end proof (3-4 weeks)\n9\t\n10\t**Goal:** prove that the core loop works for one object type, from draw to\n11\tsaved output. Nothing else matters until this works.\n12\t\n13\t### In scope\n14\t\n15\t1. A project model that serialises to disk and reloads deterministically\n16\t2. A minimal editor shell — functional, not polished — with a 2D canvas\n17\t3. Project creation with coordinate system setup (origin, true north)\n18\t4. RTG_BLOCK as the only drawable object type\n19\t5. RTG_BLOCK configuration dialog matching the prototype\n20\t6. The extraction contract implementation for RTG_BLOCK per\n21\t   `extraction-registry/RTG_BLOCK.md`\n22\t7. {"parentUuid":"20d69add-86e8-474e-afac-34aaf1afcaa7","isSidechain":false,"message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-7","id":"msg_01EHdGjX4iAo9Sb7ZGWDCbsJ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01B9gTSMxxv9sEnrtdX69jA6","name":"Read","input":{"file_path":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\001-coordinate-system.md"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":"tool_use","stop_sequence":null,"stop_details":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":11698,"cache_read_input_tokens":46044,"output_tokens":486,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":11698,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[{"input_tokens":1,"output_tokens":486,"cache_read_input_tokens":46044,"cache_creation_input_tokens":11698,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":11698},"type":"message"}],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CaKRXjzMfCa8QHcMbyjC2","type":"assistant","uuid":"63389a77-6637-4e52-bbf4-7408b3e47613","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:34.781Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}
{"parentUuid":"63389a77-6637-4e52-bbf4-7408b3e47613","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01B9gTSMxxv9sEnrtdX69jA6","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR-001 — Coordinate System Strategy\n2\t\n3\t**Status:** ACCEPTED\n4\t**Date:** 2026-04-16\n5\t\n6\t## Context\n7\t\n8\tThe system combines geospatial basemap display with precision engineering\n9\tgeometry. Web Mercator screen coordinates distort distances and angles. Every\n10\tthroughput calculation, costing formula, and constraint check must be\n11\tmetrically accurate.\n12\t\n13\tPort planners work with real dimensions: a 250m maximum RTG block length, a\n14\t6.0m minimum truck lane width, a 14m underkeel clearance. Computing any of\n15\tthese in geographic or screen coordinates produces errors that compound across\n16\tthe derivation pipeline.\n17\t\n18\t## Options considered\n19\t\n20\t**A. All geometry in WGS84 throughout.** Simple storage, but all engineering\n21\tmath must convert to metric on every operation. Easy to get wrong. Distance\n22\tcalculations between WGS84 points require proper geodesic math that is often\n23\tskipped in favour of approximations.\n24\t\n25\t**B. All geometry in project-local metric plane. Basemap is a view-only\n26\tconcern.** Engineering math is native and straightforward. Basemap integration\n27\trequires a transformation layer but only at the view boundary. WGS84 is used\n28\tfor import/export and API display only.\n29\t\n30\t**C. Dual storage: WGS84 for persistence, metric for computation.** Doubles\n31\tstorage complexity, introduces synchronization concerns, creates opportunities\n32\tfor the two representations to drift.\n33\t\n34\t## Decision\n35\t\n36\t**Option B.**\n37\t\n38\tEvery project stores a coordinate system record:\n39\t\n40\t```typescript\n41\tinterface ProjectCoordinateSystem {\n42\t  origin_lat: number;            // WGS84 latitude of project origin\n43\t  origin_lng: number;            // WGS84 longitude of project origin\n44\t  true_north_rotation: number;   // degrees clockwise from grid north\n45\t  utm_zone: string;              // e.g. \"40N\"\n46\t}\n47\t```\n48\t\n49\tAll element geometry is stored in project-local X/Y metres from the origin.\n50\tAll engineering computation happens in this system. Conversion to WGS84\n51\thappens at the API boundary when needed for display or export.\n52\t\n53\tPostGIS queries use a materialized WGS84 view for spatial indexing, but the\n54\tauthoritative store is project-local metric.\n55\t\n56\t## Consequences\n57\t\n58\t- All geometric math — fillet radii, setback distances, block lengths — is\n59\t  metrically accurate and straightforward to implement.\n60\t- Basemap alignment is a display concern handled at the view layer.\n61\t- Adding raster reference layers (bathymetry, survey data) fits cleanly:\n62\t  rasters are registered against the project coordinate system at import.\n63\t- Origin is chosen at project creation and immutable. Moving it later would\n64\t  invalidate all stored geometry (rare, would be a deliberate transformation\n65\t  operation).\n66\t- Cross-project spatial queries require transformation through WGS84.\n67\t\n68\t## What this makes harder\n69\t\n70\t- Projects cannot silently share geometry without coordinate system alignment.\n71\t- If the origin is chosen poorly (too far from the main site), metric\n72\t  coordinates become large and lose floating point precision at the edges.\n73\t  Good default: require origin within 1km of the main drawing area.\n74\t- Users who think geographically (lat/lng) rather than metrically need\n75\t  conversion support in the UI.\n76\t"}]},"uuid":"d06d5be6-a731-4296-a9c8-5035111cba53","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:34.786Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\001-coordinate-system.md","content":"# ADR-001 — Coordinate System Strategy\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-16\n\n## Context\n\nThe system combines geospatial basemap display with precision engineering\ngeometry. Web Mercator screen coordinates distort distances and angles. Every\nthroughput calculation, costing formula, and constraint check must be\nmetrically accurate.\n\nPort planners work with real dimensions: a 250m maximum RTG block length, a\n6.0m minimum truck lane width, a 14m underkeel clearance. Computing any of\nthese in geographic or screen coordinates produces errors that compound across\nthe derivation pipeline.\n\n## Options considered\n\n**A. All geometry in WGS84 throughout.** Simple storage, but all engineering\nmath must convert to metric on every operation. Easy to get wrong. Distance\ncalculations between WGS84 points require proper geodesic math that is often\nskipped in favour of approximations.\n\n**B. All geometry in project-local metric plane. Basemap is a view-only\nconcern.** Engineering math is native and straightforward. Basemap integration\nrequires a transformation layer but only at the view boundary. WGS84 is used\nfor import/export and API display only.\n\n**C. Dual storage: WGS84 for persistence, metric for computation.** Doubles\nstorage complexity, introduces synchronization concerns, creates opportunities\nfor the two representations to drift.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Option B.**\n\nEvery project stores a coordinate system record:\n\n```typescript\ninterface ProjectCoordinateSystem {\n  origin_lat: number;            // WGS84 latitude of project origin\n  origin_lng: number;            // WGS84 longitude of project origin\n  true_north_rotation: number;   // degrees clockwise from grid north\n  utm_zone: string;              // e.g. \"40N\"\n}\n```\n\nAll element geometry is stored in project-local X/Y metres from the origin.\nAll engineering computation happens in this system. Conversion to WGS84\nhappens at the API boundary when needed for display or export.\n\nPostGIS queries use a materialized WGS84 view for spatial indexing, but the\nauthoritative store is project-local metric.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- All geometric math — fillet radii, setback distances, block lengths — is\n  metrically accurate and straightforward to implement.\n- Basemap alignment is a display concern handled at the view layer.\n- Adding raster reference layers (bathymetry, survey data) fits cleanly:\n  rasters are registered against the project coordinate system at import.\n- Origin is chosen at project creation and immutable. Moving it later would\n  invalidate all stored geometry (rare, would be a deliberate transformation\n  operation).\n- Cross-project spatial queries require transformation through WGS84.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- Projects cannot silently share geometry without coordinate system alignment.\n- If the origin is chosen poorly (too far from the main site), metric\n  coordinates become large and lose floating point precision at the edges.\n  Good default: require origin within 1km of the main drawing area.\n- Users who think geographically (lat/lng) rather than metrically need\n  conversion support in the UI.\n","numLines":76,"startLine":1,"totalLines":76}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"63389a77-6637-4e52-bbf4-7408b3e47613","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"3d782a96-40a1-42e7-bef8-31b177b20861","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01RAWLBAvfuiaCnsDhCXz3Vd","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR-004 — Parameter Extraction Contract\n2\t\n3\t**Status:** ACCEPTED\n4\t**Date:** 2026-04-16\n5\t\n6\t## Context\n7\t\n8\tThe throughput model, costing engine, and validation engine all need\n9\toperational quantities derived from object geometry and parameters. A berth has a crane\n11\tposition count.\n12\t\n13\tIf this derivation is scattered across analysis code, the system becomes\n14\tuntestable, unstable, and impossible to audit. Extractors run\n29\tat save time.** Clean contract. Always-fresh results. Expensive on every\n30\tsave for complex projects.\n31\t\n32\t**C. Typed extractors run lazily on demand with a versioned cache keyed by\n33\tobject geometry fingerprint.** Clean contract plus performance discipline.\n34\t\n35\t## Decision\n36\t\n37\t**Option C** — typed extractors with lazy evaluation and fingerprint-keyed\n38\tcaching.\n39\t\n40\tEach `ObjectType` registers a `QuantityExtractor`:\n41\t\n42\t```typescript\n43\tinterface QuantityExtractor {\n44\t  object_type: ObjectType;\n45\t  version: string;                     // semver, bumped when formula changes\n46\t\n47\t  extract(\n48\t    geometry: ProjectGeometry,\n49\t    parameters: ObjectParameters,\n50\t    scenario_overrides: ScenarioOverrides\n51\t  ): QuantityBundle;\n52\t}\n53\t\n54\tinterface QuantityBundle {\n55\t  // Physical quantities\n56\t  gross_area_m2?: number;\n57\t  net_area_m2?: number;\n58\t  length_m?: number;\n59\t  volume_m3?: number;\n60\t\n61\t  // Operational quantities\n62\t  teu_slots?: number;\n63\t  crane_positions?: number;\n64\t  truck_lane_length_m?: number;\n65\t  berth_length_m?: number;\n66\t\n67\t  // Equipment quantities\n68\t  rtg_count?: number;\n69\t  gate_lanes?: number;\n70\t\n71\t  // Extensible per object type\n72\t  [key: string]: number | string | undefined;\n73\t\n74\t  // Metadata\n75\t  extractor_version: string;\n76\t  extraction_timestamp: timestamp;\n77\t  warnings: ExtractionWarning[];\n78\t}\n79\t```\n80\t\n81\t**Storage:** extracted bundles are stored in `object_quantities`, keyed by\n82\t`(object_id, scenario_id, extractor_version)`. Invalidated when object\n83\tgeometry or parameters change.\n84\t\n85\t**Scenario overrides:** a scenario can override specific quantity values with\n86\texplicit provenance:\n87\t\n88\t```typescript\n89\tinterface QuantityOverride {\n90\t  object_id: UUID;\n91\t  scenario_id: UUID;\n92\t  quantity_key: string;                // e.g. \"teu_slots\"\n93\t  original_value: number;\n94\t  override_value: number;\n95\t  override_reason: string;             // required\n96\t  overridden_by: UUID;\n97\t  overridden_at: timestamp;\n98\t  extractor_version: string;           // version at time of override\n99\t}\n100\t```\n101\t\n102\t**Governance:** the registry of valid extractors lives in\n103\t`docs/extraction-registry/`. An object type cannot enter production without\n104\ta registry entry. Changing a formula requires bumping the extractor version\n105\tand a migration note.\n106\t\n107\t## Consequences\n108\t\n109\t- Every throughput and cost output is traceable to a specific object,\n110\t  extractor version, and scenario.\n111\t- Changing an extractor formula is a deliberate versioned event.\n112\t- Scenario overrides are explicit and reasoned.\n113\t- The extraction layer is unit-testable independently of the editor.\n114\t- \"Why did we get 18,200 TEU?\" resolves to a specific extractor version and\n115\t  input set.\n116\t- Multiple scenarios over the same geometry reuse the cache except where they\n117\t  override.\n118\t\n119\t## What this makes harder\n120\t\n121\t- Adding a new object type now requires a registry entry, an extractor\n122\t  implementation, and test cases before it can enter the system.\n123\t- Changing a formula requires version bumping and triggers recomputation of\n124\t  stored bundles across all projects.\n125\t- The cost analysis and throughput model cannot take shortcuts by reaching\n126\t  into geometry directly — they must go through the extraction layer.\n127\t"}]},"uuid":"665b3c7a-620c-4219-8c5a-297e604b4578","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:35.209Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\004-parameter-extraction.md","content":"# ADR-004 — Parameter Extraction Contract\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-16\n\n## Context\n\nThe throughput model, costing engine, and validation engine all need\noperational quantities derived from object geometry and parameters. An RTG\nblock has a TEU slot count. A road has a pavement area. A berth has a crane\nposition count.\n\nIf this derivation is scattered across analysis code, the system becomes\nuntestable, unstable, and impossible to audit. When a throughput number\nchanges by 5%, nobody can trace why.\n\nThis is the seam between spatial engineering (what planners draw) and\noperations analysis (what the commercial model consumes). It is the most\nconsequential interface in the system.\n\n## Options considered\n\n**A. Analysis code reads geometry directly and derives what it needs.**\nFastest to implement initially. Creates implicit, scattered formulas.\nDuplication across throughput and costing modules. No version control over\nthe formulas. \"Why did we get 18,200 TEU?\" has no clean answer.\n\n**B. Each object type registers a typed extractor function. Extractors run\nat save time.** Clean contract. Always-fresh results. Expensive on every\nsave for complex projects.\n\n**C. Typed extractors run lazily on demand with a versioned cache keyed by\nobject geometry fingerprint.** Clean contract plus performance discipline.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Option C** — typed extractors with lazy evaluation and fingerprint-keyed\ncaching.\n\nEach `ObjectType` registers a `QuantityExtractor`:\n\n```typescript\ninterface QuantityExtractor {\n  object_type: ObjectType;\n  version: string;                     // semver, bumped when formula changes\n\n  extract(\n    geometry: ProjectGeometry,\n    parameters: ObjectParameters,\n    scenario_overrides: ScenarioOverrides\n  ): QuantityBundle;\n}\n\ninterface QuantityBundle {\n  // Physical quantities\n  gross_area_m2?: number;\n  net_area_m2?: number;\n  length_m?: number;\n  volume_m3?: number;\n\n  // Operational quantities\n  teu_slots?: number;\n  crane_positions?: number;\n  truck_lane_length_m?: number;\n  berth_length_m?: number;\n\n  // Equipment quantities\n  rtg_count?: number;\n  gate_lanes?: number;\n\n  // Extensible per object type\n  [key: string]: number | string | undefined;\n\n  // Metadata\n  extractor_version: string;\n  extraction_timestamp: timestamp;\n  warnings: ExtractionWarning[];\n}\n```\n\n**Storage:** extracted bundles are stored in `object_quantities`, keyed by\n`(object_id, scenario_id, extractor_version)`. Invalidated when object\ngeometry or parameters change.\n\n**Scenario overrides:** a scenario can override specific quantity values with\nexplicit provenance:\n\n```typescript\ninterface QuantityOverride {\n  object_id: UUID;\n  scenario_id: UUID;\n  quantity_key: string;                // e.g. \"teu_slots\"\n  original_value: number;\n  override_value: number;\n  override_reason: string;             // required\n  overridden_by: UUID;\n  overridden_at: timestamp;\n  extractor_version: string;           // version at time of override\n}\n```\n\n**Governance:** the registry of valid extractors lives in\n`docs/extraction-registry/`. An object type cannot enter production without\na registry entry. Changing a formula requires bumping the extractor version\nand a migration note.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Every throughput and cost output is traceable to a specific object,\n  extractor version, and scenario.\n- Changing an extractor formula is a deliberate versioned event.\n- Scenario overrides are explicit and reasoned.\n- The extraction layer is unit-testable independently of the editor.\n- \"Why did we get 18,200 TEU?\" resolves to a specific extractor version and\n  input set.\n- Multiple scenarios over the same geometry reuse the cache except where they\n  override.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- Adding a new object type now requires a registry entry, an extractor\n  implementation, and test cases before it can enter the system.\n- Changing a formula requires version bumping and triggers recomputation of\n  stored bundles across all projects.\n- The cost analysis and throughput model cannot take shortcuts by reaching\n  into geometry directly — they must go through the extraction layer.\n","numLines":127,"startLine":1,"totalLines":127}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"3d782a96-40a1-42e7-bef8-31b177b20861","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"9b3a2cad-1033-48e8-a018-bb72360990be","isSidechain":false,"promptId":"36ea3f62-4d92-4fa4-9679-c49d23694d30","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013RPpPb35oqGC9673XtrQNW","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# ADR-015 — Project Store and State Management Scope\n2\t\n3\t**Status:** ACCEPTED\n4\t**Date:** 2026-04-21\n5\t\n6\t## Context\n7\t\n8\tMilestone 1.2 introduces the first stateful machinery in the codebase.\n9\tADR-012 pinned **Zustand + `zundo`** as the state-management stack.\n10\tADR-010 defines the **project sync model** (operation log, object-level\n11\tlast-write-wins). ADR-014 defines **persistence** (IndexedDB + `idb` in\n12\tM1; Postgres + PostGIS server-side later). None of these ADRs pins the\n13\t*specifics of how the project store is composed*:\n14\t\n15\t- Which parts of state are captured by `zundo`'s undo history?\n16\t- Is Immer middleware adopted for reducer ergonomics?\n17\t- Is `zustand-persist` (or any automatic persistence middleware) allowed?\n18\t- How is `@portplanner/project-store-react` declared so it does not pull\n19\t  in its own React instance?\n20\t\n21\tEach decision is **load-bearing**:\n22\t- Wrong `zundo` scope corrupts the Ctrl+Z UX (e.g., Ctrl+Z undoes a\n23\t  *selection change* rather than a *drawing action*).\n24\t- Wrong persistence approach fights ADR-014's canonical-JSON + IndexedDB\n25\t  story by owning a second persistence channel.\n26\t- Wrong reducer discipline makes the codebase noisy and bug-prone when\n27\t  mutating nested project structures.\n28\t- Wrong React packaging causes the \"multiple React copies detected\"\n29\t  runtime error that breaks hooks.\n30\t\n31\tThis ADR scopes all four. It does not supersede ADR-012 (which remains\n32\tthe authority on Zustand as the library choice) — it constrains the\n33\tusage of that library.\n34\t\n35\tLanded alongside the GR-3 extension that adds `packages/project-store`\n36\tand `packages/project-store-react` to the allowed dependency graph (see\n37\t`docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md` §0.4).\n38\t\n39\t## Options considered\n40\t\n41\t### 1. `zundo` undo-history scope\n42\t\n43\t- **A. Project slice only.** Only mutations to the `Project` value are\n44\t  recorded. Selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom are excluded.\n45\t- **B. Entire store.** Every state change becomes an undo step.\n46\t- **C. Opt-in per slice.** Middleware wrapping decides per slice.\n47\t\n48\t### 2. Immer middleware adoption\n49\t\n50\t- **A. Adopt via `zustand/middleware` immer helper.** Reducers can write\n51\t  `draft.objects[id] = newObj` instead of spreading manually.\n52\t- **B. Manual spreads only.** `set({ ...state, objects: { ...state.objects, [id]: newObj } })`.\n53\t- **C. Hand-written deep-clone helpers.** Worst of both worlds.\n54\t\n55\t### 3. Third-party persistence middleware\n56\t\n57\t- **A. Ban `zustand-persist` and any auto-persistence.** ADR-014's\n58\t  IndexedDB + `idb` wrapper is the sole persistence authority.\n59\t  Save/load triggered explicitly via UI.\n60\t- **B. Adopt `zustand-persist`.** Middleware automatically syncs to\n61\t  `localStorage` / `sessionStorage` / IndexedDB.\n62\t- **C. Hybrid.** Use `zustand-persist` for UI state; ADR-014 for the\n63\t  project.\n64\t\n65\t### 4. React packaging for `project-store-react`\n66\t\n67\t- **A. React as `peerDependency` only.** `project-store-react` declares\n68\t  `\"peerDependencies\": { \"react\": \"...\" }` and does NOT declare\n69\t  `\"dependencies\": { \"react\": \"...\" }`. The consumer (apps/web)\n70\t  provides React.\n71\t- **B. React as direct dependency.** `project-store-react` bundles its\n72\t  own React.\n73\t- **C. React as both.** Defensive but confusing.\n74\t\n75\t## Decision\n76\t\n77\t| # | Area | Choice | Rationale |\n78\t|---|------|--------|-----------|\n79\t| 1 | `zundo` scope | **Project slice only.** Selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom, hover, snap preview, dimension preview — all EXCLUDED from history. | Ctrl+Z expected semantics: \"undo the last drawing action I took\", not \"undo my selection change\". Tracking ephemeral UI state creates noise, surprise, and broken mental models. Project mutations (object create/update/delete, classification change, parameter edit, ownership transition) are the true undo units per ADR-010's operation log. |\n80\t| 2 | Immer | **Adopt** via `zustand/middleware` immer. | `Project` is deeply nested (objects map, per-object `parameters` JSONB, nested coordinate configs). Manual spreads get verbose and error-prone for nested updates. Immer's draft-mutation style reads cleanly and eliminates a class of \"forgot to spread this level\" bugs. Bundle cost ~8 KB gzipped; acceptable. |\n81\t| 3 | Persistence | **BAN `zustand-persist` and all auto-persistence middleware.** ADR-014 (IndexedDB + `idb` + canonical JSON) is the sole persistence authority. Save/load is triggered explicitly from UI; no middleware writes to any storage on state change. | `zustand-persist` aggressively owns storage channels (`localStorage` by default, optionally IndexedDB). Letting it run alongside ADR-014's canonical-JSON + per-project-ID IndexedDB store would create two persistence writers with different serialisation conventions, guaranteed drift. The IndexedDB write step needs access to the canonical serialiser defined in `packages/domain` — `zustand-persist` can't call that. Explicit save triggers are correct for a CAD-like tool anyway: users expect \"Save\" to mean something. |\n82\t| 4 | React in `project-store-react` | **`peerDependencies` only.** `package.json` lists React ONLY under `peerDependencies`; NEVER under `dependencies`. | Prevents `project-store-react` from pulling in its own React instance at a different version from apps/web's React. Dual React instances break hooks (the \"invalid hook call\" / \"multiple React copies\" error). `peerDependencies` signals \"the consumer provides React; versions must agree.\" |\n83\t\n84\t### Concrete usage contract\n85\t\n86\t- The project store is defined in `packages/project-store/src/` as a\n87\t  vanilla Zustand store (imported from `zustand/vanilla`), wrapped by\n88\t  `zundo`'s middleware scoped to the `project` slice only, and by\n89\t  `zustand/middleware`'s `immer` helper for the same slice.\n90\t- The store exposes `subscribe(listener)` and `getState()` — the vanilla\n91\t  Zustand API. Actions (`createNewProject`, `hydrateProject`, `markSaved`,\n92\t  and later `placeObject` / `moveObject` / etc.) are plain functions also\n93\t  exported from `packages/project-store`. **Canvas paint loops and other\n94\t  non-React consumers import from `packages/project-store` directly** —\n95\t  they do NOT need the React bindings.\n96\t- `packages/project-store-react/src/` exposes React hooks that wrap the\n97\t  same vanilla store via `useSyncExternalStore`:\n98\t  - `useProject()` → the current `Project`\n99\t  - `useProjectId()` → the current project id\n100\t  - `useObjectById(id)` → a specific object (selector pattern)\n101\t  - `useIsDirty()` → dirty flag\n102\t  - `useLastSavedAt()` → last-save timestamp\n103\t  - additional selectors land per milestone need\n104\t\n105\t  **Hooks live only in `project-store-react`. Actions live only in\n106\t  `project-store`. Consumers import from where each lives.** No re-export\n107\t  pattern is required or recommended.\n108\t- UI state (selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom) in M1.2 is\n109\t  **not yet in scope** because the canvas does not exist. When added in\n110\t  M1.3, it lives in a SEPARATE store (`packages/ui-state/` or similar)\n111\t  with its own semantics — no `zundo`, no Immer required, no persistence.\n112\t  That decision gets its own ADR when the need is real.\n113\t- Persistence (save/load) is implemented in `apps/web/src/persistence/`\n114\t  per ADR-014. It calls `projectStore.getState()` to read the current\n115\t  project and the canonical serializer from `packages/domain` to encode\n116\t  it. There is no persistence middleware inside the store package.\n117\t\n118\t### Test isolation\n119\t\n120\tModule-level singletons (how Zustand is typically exported) share state\n121\tacross tests. The project-store MUST expose a reset helper:\n122\t\n123\t```ts\n124\t// packages/project-store/src/index.ts\n125\texport function resetProjectStoreForTests(): void {\n126\t  projectStore.setState(createInitialProjectState(), true);\n127\t}\n128\t```\n129\t\n130\tTests call it in `beforeEach`. This is the official Zustand-recommended\n131\tpattern for singleton stores.\n132\t\n133\t## Consequences\n134\t\n135\t- Ctrl+Z behaves as users expect: only project-level drawing / edit\n136\t  actions are undoable. Selection, tool switches, and viewport pans are\n137\t  not tracked.\n138\t- Reducer code in `project-store` stays readable via Immer mutations.\n139\t- Persistence is single-sourced through ADR-014; no drift between two\n140\t  storage writers.\n141\t- `project-store-react` is safely importable from any package (apps/web,\n142\t  editor-2d React components, viewer-3d React components) without causing\n143\t  dual-React runtime errors.\n144\t- GR-3 extension ensures canvas paint loops never accidentally pull\n145\t  React through the store layer.\n146\t- The vanilla/React split mirrors Zustand's own `zustand/vanilla` +\n147\t  `zustand` entry pattern and the Redux + react-redux pattern; imports\n148\t  make consumer intent explicit.\n149\t\n150\t## What this makes harder\n151\t\n152\t- If a future milestone decides Ctrl+Z should also revert a selection\n153\t  change (unlikely but possible for specific UX patterns), a superseding\n154\t  ADR is required — plus either widening `zundo`'s scope or adding a\n155\t  secondary undo stack for UI state. Both are non-trivial.\n156\t- Immer adds ~8 KB gzipped to the bundle. Acceptable; noted.\n157\t- Banning `zustand-persist` means we forgo its conveniences\n158\t  (`partialize`, `version` migrations, `storage` abstraction). We must\n159\t  let `apps/web/src/persistence/` handle them via ADR-014's wrapper.\n160\t  Migrations are deferred to when schema versioning becomes real.\n161\t- `peerDependencies` discipline means adding `project-store-react` to\n162\t  any new app requires that app to also install React — a harmless\n163\t  duplication in `package.json` that pnpm workspaces handle naturally.\n164\t- Two workspace packages (`project-store` + `project-store-react`)\n165\t  instead of one. ~6 extra scaffold files total; amortised benefit via\n166\t  enforced vanilla-vs-React boundary.\n167\t\n168\t## Cross-references\n169\t\n170\t- **ADR-010** Project Sync and Offline Model — defines the operation\n171\t  log structure that `zundo` captures as undo steps.\n172\t- **ADR-012** Technology Stack — pins Zustand + `zundo` + Immer as\n173\t  libraries; this ADR scopes their application.\n174\t- **ADR-014** Persistence Architecture — sole authority for project\n175\t  save/load. `zustand-persist` ban exists to keep that authority\n176\t  un-contested.\n177\t- **`docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md` §0.4 (GR-3)**\n178\t  — lists `packages/project-store` and `packages/project-store-react`\n179\t  in the allowed dependency graph with the canvas-no-React grep gate.\n180\t\n181\t## Changelog\n182\t\n183\t| Version | Date | Change |\n184\t|---|---|---|\n185\t| 1.1.0 | 2026-04-22 | Renamed \"document store\" → \"project store\" + \"doc-store\" packages → \"project-store\" packages (also ADR title, body, cross-refs). Dropped the action re-export pattern from the concrete usage contract — hooks live only in `project-store-react`, actions live only in `project-store`, consumers import from where each lives. Semantics unchanged. |\n186\t| 1.0.0 | 2026-04-21 | Initial ADR. Scopes `zundo` to project slice only; adopts Immer; bans `zustand-persist`; mandates React as peerDependency in `project-store-react`. |\n187\t"}]},"uuid":"e0930e23-38f1-4bd7-b257-41810a23ef88","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:35.636Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\015-project-store-state-management.md","content":"# ADR-015 — Project Store and State Management Scope\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-21\n\n## Context\n\nMilestone 1.2 introduces the first stateful machinery in the codebase.\nADR-012 pinned **Zustand + `zundo`** as the state-management stack.\nADR-010 defines the **project sync model** (operation log, object-level\nlast-write-wins). ADR-014 defines **persistence** (IndexedDB + `idb` in\nM1; Postgres + PostGIS server-side later). None of these ADRs pins the\n*specifics of how the project store is composed*:\n\n- Which parts of state are captured by `zundo`'s undo history?\n- Is Immer middleware adopted for reducer ergonomics?\n- Is `zustand-persist` (or any automatic persistence middleware) allowed?\n- How is `@portplanner/project-store-react` declared so it does not pull\n  in its own React instance?\n\nEach decision is **load-bearing**:\n- Wrong `zundo` scope corrupts the Ctrl+Z UX (e.g., Ctrl+Z undoes a\n  *selection change* rather than a *drawing action*).\n- Wrong persistence approach fights ADR-014's canonical-JSON + IndexedDB\n  story by owning a second persistence channel.\n- Wrong reducer discipline makes the codebase noisy and bug-prone when\n  mutating nested project structures.\n- Wrong React packaging causes the \"multiple React copies detected\"\n  runtime error that breaks hooks.\n\nThis ADR scopes all four. It does not supersede ADR-012 (which remains\nthe authority on Zustand as the library choice) — it constrains the\nusage of that library.\n\nLanded alongside the GR-3 extension that adds `packages/project-store`\nand `packages/project-store-react` to the allowed dependency graph (see\n`docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md` §0.4).\n\n## Options considered\n\n### 1. `zundo` undo-history scope\n\n- **A. Project slice only.** Only mutations to the `Project` value are\n  recorded. Selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom are excluded.\n- **B. Entire store.** Every state change becomes an undo step.\n- **C. Opt-in per slice.** Middleware wrapping decides per slice.\n\n### 2. Immer middleware adoption\n\n- **A. Adopt via `zustand/middleware` immer helper.** Reducers can write\n  `draft.objects[id] = newObj` instead of spreading manually.\n- **B. Manual spreads only.** `set({ ...state, objects: { ...state.objects, [id]: newObj } })`.\n- **C. Hand-written deep-clone helpers.** Worst of both worlds.\n\n### 3. Third-party persistence middleware\n\n- **A. Ban `zustand-persist` and any auto-persistence.** ADR-014's\n  IndexedDB + `idb` wrapper is the sole persistence authority.\n  Save/load triggered explicitly via UI.\n- **B. Adopt `zustand-persist`.** Middleware automatically syncs to\n  `localStorage` / `sessionStorage` / IndexedDB.\n- **C. Hybrid.** Use `zustand-persist` for UI state; ADR-014 for the\n  project.\n\n### 4. React packaging for `project-store-react`\n\n- **A. React as `peerDependency` only.** `project-store-react` declares\n  `\"peerDependencies\": { \"react\": \"...\" }` and does NOT declare\n  `\"dependencies\": { \"react\": \"...\" }`. The consumer (apps/web)\n  provides React.\n- **B. React as direct dependency.** `project-store-react` bundles its\n  own React.\n- **C. React as both.** Defensive but confusing.\n\n## Decision\n\n| # | Area | Choice | Rationale |\n|---|------|--------|-----------|\n| 1 | `zundo` scope | **Project slice only.** Selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom, hover, snap preview, dimension preview — all EXCLUDED from history. | Ctrl+Z expected semantics: \"undo the last drawing action I took\", not \"undo my selection change\". Tracking ephemeral UI state creates noise, surprise, and broken mental models. Project mutations (object create/update/delete, classification change, parameter edit, ownership transition) are the true undo units per ADR-010's operation log. |\n| 2 | Immer | **Adopt** via `zustand/middleware` immer. | `Project` is deeply nested (objects map, per-object `parameters` JSONB, nested coordinate configs). Manual spreads get verbose and error-prone for nested updates. Immer's draft-mutation style reads cleanly and eliminates a class of \"forgot to spread this level\" bugs. Bundle cost ~8 KB gzipped; acceptable. |\n| 3 | Persistence | **BAN `zustand-persist` and all auto-persistence middleware.** ADR-014 (IndexedDB + `idb` + canonical JSON) is the sole persistence authority. Save/load is triggered explicitly from UI; no middleware writes to any storage on state change. | `zustand-persist` aggressively owns storage channels (`localStorage` by default, optionally IndexedDB). Letting it run alongside ADR-014's canonical-JSON + per-project-ID IndexedDB store would create two persistence writers with different serialisation conventions, guaranteed drift. The IndexedDB write step needs access to the canonical serialiser defined in `packages/domain` — `zustand-persist` can't call that. Explicit save triggers are correct for a CAD-like tool anyway: users expect \"Save\" to mean something. |\n| 4 | React in `project-store-react` | **`peerDependencies` only.** `package.json` lists React ONLY under `peerDependencies`; NEVER under `dependencies`. | Prevents `project-store-react` from pulling in its own React instance at a different version from apps/web's React. Dual React instances break hooks (the \"invalid hook call\" / \"multiple React copies\" error). `peerDependencies` signals \"the consumer provides React; versions must agree.\" |\n\n### Concrete usage contract\n\n- The project store is defined in `packages/project-store/src/` as a\n  vanilla Zustand store (imported from `zustand/vanilla`), wrapped by\n  `zundo`'s middleware scoped to the `project` slice only, and by\n  `zustand/middleware`'s `immer` helper for the same slice.\n- The store exposes `subscribe(listener)` and `getState()` — the vanilla\n  Zustand API. Actions (`createNewProject`, `hydrateProject`, `markSaved`,\n  and later `placeObject` / `moveObject` / etc.) are plain functions also\n  exported from `packages/project-store`. **Canvas paint loops and other\n  non-React consumers import from `packages/project-store` directly** —\n  they do NOT need the React bindings.\n- `packages/project-store-react/src/` exposes React hooks that wrap the\n  same vanilla store via `useSyncExternalStore`:\n  - `useProject()` → the current `Project`\n  - `useProjectId()` → the current project id\n  - `useObjectById(id)` → a specific object (selector pattern)\n  - `useIsDirty()` → dirty flag\n  - `useLastSavedAt()` → last-save timestamp\n  - additional selectors land per milestone need\n\n  **Hooks live only in `project-store-react`. Actions live only in\n  `project-store`. Consumers import from where each lives.** No re-export\n  pattern is required or recommended.\n- UI state (selection, active tool, viewport pan/zoom) in M1.2 is\n  **not yet in scope** because the canvas does not exist. When added in\n  M1.3, it lives in a SEPARATE store (`packages/ui-state/` or similar)\n  with its own semantics — no `zundo`, no Immer required, no persistence.\n  That decision gets its own ADR when the need is real.\n- Persistence (save/load) is implemented in `apps/web/src/persistence/`\n  per ADR-014. It calls `projectStore.getState()` to read the current\n  project and the canonical serializer from `packages/domain` to encode\n  it. There is no persistence middleware inside the store package.\n\n### Test isolation\n\nModule-level singletons (how Zustand is typically exported) share state\nacross tests. The project-store MUST expose a reset helper:\n\n```ts\n// packages/project-store/src/index.ts\nexport function resetProjectStoreForTests(): void {\n  projectStore.setState(createInitialProjectState(), true);\n}\n```\n\nTests call it in `beforeEach`. This is the official Zustand-recommended\npattern for singleton stores.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Ctrl+Z behaves as users expect: only project-level drawing / edit\n  actions are undoable. Selection, tool switches, and viewport pans are\n  not tracked.\n- Reducer code in `project-store` stays readable via Immer mutations.\n- Persistence is single-sourced through ADR-014; no drift between two\n  storage writers.\n- `project-store-react` is safely importable from any package (apps/web,\n  editor-2d React components, viewer-3d React components) without causing\n  dual-React runtime errors.\n- GR-3 extension ensures canvas paint loops never accidentally pull\n  React through the store layer.\n- The vanilla/React split mirrors Zustand's own `zustand/vanilla` +\n  `zustand` entry pattern and the Redux + react-redux pattern; imports\n  make consumer intent explicit.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- If a future milestone decides Ctrl+Z should also revert a selection\n  change (unlikely but possible for specific UX patterns), a superseding\n  ADR is required — plus either widening `zundo`'s scope or adding a\n  secondary undo stack for UI state. Both are non-trivial.\n- Immer adds ~8 KB gzipped to the bundle. Acceptable; noted.\n- Banning `zustand-persist` means we forgo its conveniences\n  (`partialize`, `version` migrations, `storage` abstraction). We must\n  let `apps/web/src/persistence/` handle them via ADR-014's wrapper.\n  Migrations are deferred to when schema versioning becomes real.\n- `peerDependencies` discipline means adding `project-store-react` to\n  any new app requires that app to also install React — a harmless\n  duplication in `package.json` that pnpm workspaces handle naturally.\n- Two workspace packages (`project-store` + `project-store-react`)\n  instead of one. ~6 extra scaffold files total; amortised benefit via\n  enforced vanilla-vs-React boundary.\n\n## Cross-references\n\n- **ADR-010** Project Sync and Offline Model — defines the operation\n  log structure that `zundo` captures as undo steps.\n- **ADR-012** Technology Stack — pins Zustand + `zundo` + Immer as\n  libraries; this ADR scopes their application.\n- **ADR-014** Persistence Architecture — sole authority for project\n  save/load. `zustand-persist` ban exists to keep that authority\n  un-contested.\n- **`docs/procedures/Claude/00-architecture-contract.md` §0.4 (GR-3)**\n  — lists `packages/project-store` and `packages/project-store-react`\n  in the allowed dependency graph with the canvas-no-React grep gate.\n\n## Changelog\n\n| Version | Date | Change |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1.1.0 | 2026-04-22 | Renamed \"document store\" → \"project store\" + \"doc-store\" packages → \"project-store\" packages (also ADR title, body, cross-refs). Dropped the action re-export pattern from the concrete usage contract — hooks live only in `project-store-react`, actions live only in `project-store`, consumers import from where each lives. Semantics unchanged. |\n| 1.0.0 | 2026-04-21 | Initial ADR. Scopes `zundo` to project slice only; adopts Immer; bans `zustand-persist`; mandates React as peerDependency in `project-store-react`. |\n","numLines":187,"startLine":1,"totalLines":187}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9b3a2cad-1033-48e8-a018-bb72360990be","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

Every\nobject type that contributes to analysis has an entry here. Implementation\nfollows the specification; specification does not follow implementation.\n\nSee ADR-004 for the architectural decision underlying this registry.\n\n## Files\n\n- [`RTG_BLOCK.md`](RTG_BLOCK.md) — Rubber-tyred gantry container stack block\n- [`ROAD.md`](ROAD.md) — Road segment\n- [`BUILDING.md`](BUILDING.md) — Building footprint with vertical extent\n- [`PAVEMENT_AREA.md`](PAVEMENT_AREA.md) — Paved surface polygon\n- [`BERTH.md`](BERTH.md) — Berth line with vessel specification\n\n## Cross-object extractors\n\n- [`YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md`](YARD_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md) — Aggregate yard\n  throughput metrics\n- [`GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md`](GATE_CAPACITY_SUMMARY.md) — Aggregate gate\n  throughput metrics\n\n## Entry format\n\nEach entry contains:\n\n```\n# OBJECT_TYPE\n\nVersion: X.Y.Z\n\n## Inputs\nList of parameters and geometry inputs the extractor consumes.\n\n## Outputs\nTyped quantities the extractor produces.\n\n## Formulas\nHow each output is computed from inputs.\n\n## Validation rules\nRules registered against this object type, with severity and threshold.\n\n## Changelog\nVersion history with reasons for bumps.\n```\n\n## Governance\n\n### Adding a new object type\n\n1. Write the registry entry (this document) first.\n2. Implement the `QuantityExtractor` class matching the specification.\n3. Register in the `ExtractorRegistry`.\n4. Write unit tests covering every output formula and every validation rule\n   including edge cases.\n5. Only then may the object type enter production.\n\n### Changing an existing extractor\n\n1. Bump the semver version in the registry entry.\n2. Add a changelog note: what changed, why, impact on stored results.\n3. All stored `QuantityBundle` records with the old version are invalidated\n   on deploy.\n4. Recomputation runs as a background job.\n5. Output values may change for existing projects — this is expected and\n   must be communicated to affected users.\n\n### Scenario overrides\n\nA scenario may override any specific output value from an extractor. The\noverride is explicit, reasoned, and traceable (see ADR-004). Overrides do\nnot change the extractor; they substitute values at the scenario level.\n\n## Versioning policy\n\n- **Patch bump (X.Y.Z → X.Y.Z+1):** bug fix to formula, same output shape.\n- **Minor bump (X.Y.0 → X.Y+1.0):** new optional output field added.\n- **Major bump (X.0.0 → X+1.0.0):** existing output field changed, removed,\n  or semantics changed.\n\nMajor bumps require an ADR documenting the reason and a migration note.\n","numLines":85,"startLine":1,"totalLines":85}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"866b6abb-4ed2-408a-8948-fecdd49a89fb","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

Moving it may trigger regeneration of dependent objects. |\n55\t| GENERATED | Deleted and replaced. |\n56\t| FROZEN | Skipped entirely. Position held fixed and treated as an obstacle by the generator. |\n57\t| DETACHED | Generator prompts user: \"X objects have manual edits. Keep edits (freeze) or regenerate?\" |\n58\t\n59\t**State transitions:**\n60\t\n61\t| From | Event | To |\n62\t|---|---|---|\n63\t| (none) | Generator creates | GENERATED |\n64\t| (none) | User draws directly | AUTHORED |\n65\t| GENERATED | User edits geometry or parameters | DETACHED |\n66\t| GENERATED | User explicitly freezes | FROZEN |\n67\t| DETACHED | User explicitly freezes | FROZEN |\n68\t| DETACHED | User accepts regeneration | (deleted, replaced by new GENERATED) |\n69\t| FROZEN | User unfreezes | GENERATED (re-evaluated on next regeneration) |\n70\t\n71\t**Mental model:** authored objects are constraints; generated objects are\n72\tconsequences. Moving a constraint freely updates its consequences. FROZEN and\n73\tDETACHED are user-facing escape hatches when the automatic consequence is\n74\tnot what the user wants.\n75\t\n76\t## Consequences\n77\t\n78\t- Users can safely tweak generated layouts without fear of silent overwrite.\n79\t- The generator always knows what it owns vs what is user-controlled.\n80\t- Warnings are targeted (only DETACHED objects trigger prompts), not blanket.\n81\t- \"Regenerate all\" is a safe, predictable operation with explicit exceptions.\n82\t- Moving an AUTHORED road automatically updates dependent GENERATED yards\n83\t  without any lock/unlock ceremony.\n84\t\n85\t## What this makes harder\n86\t\n87\t- Implementation has to maintain state transitions correctly across\n88\t  regeneration, manual edit, freeze, and unfreeze operations.\n89\t- Undo/redo must handle ownership state transitions as part of the history.\n90\t- When displaying an object, the UI must show its ownership state clearly\n91\t  (badge or outline style) so users know what kind of object they are\n92\t  interacting with.\n93\t"}]},"uuid":"b68f0edb-aa15-4ff2-b253-9a8ab4c011d2","timestamp":"2026-04-22T20:15:40.712Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"D:\\PortPlanner\\docs\\adr\\003-ownership-states.md","content":"# ADR-003 — Ownership States\n\n**Status:** ACCEPTED\n**Date:** 2026-04-16\n\n## Context\n\nThe generative layout engine creates objects automatically from user-drawn\nconstraints. Users will then want to modify generated objects manually. When\nthe constraints change, the generator must regenerate dependent objects.\n\nIf regeneration silently overwrites manual edits, users lose work and trust\nthe system. If regeneration refuses to run after any manual edit, the layout\nbecomes stale and the generative feature becomes useless.\n\nThis is the primary UX risk of a generative system.\n\n## Options considered\n\n**A. All objects equivalent; regeneration always overwrites.** Maximally\nsimple. Destroys manual work.\n\n**B. Manual edits permanently lock an object; regeneration skips locked\nobjects.** Prevents data loss but creates dead-ends: user cannot easily\nre-enable regeneration on an edited object.\n\n**C. Four explicit ownership states with defined regeneration behaviour.**\nMore complex but gives users predictable, reversible control.\n\n**D. Lock the authored bounding area; reject geometry changes until unlocked.**\nConsidered but rejected. Forces an unlock ceremony for every trivial edit to\nauthored constraints, which port planners do constantly. Creates friction on\nthe wrong side — constraints should be free, consequences should be managed.\n\n## Decision\n\n**Option C.**\n\nEvery object has an `ownership` field:\n\n```typescript\nenum OwnershipState {\n  AUTHORED    // user-drawn constraint, never touched by generator\n  GENERATED   // generator-created, no manual edits, safe to regenerate\n  FROZEN      // was generated, explicitly frozen by user\n  DETACHED    // was generated, manually edited by user\n}\n```\n\n**Regeneration rules:**\n\n| State | Behaviour on regeneration |\n|---|---|\n| AUTHORED | Never touched by generator. Moving it may trigger regeneration of dependent objects. |\n| GENERATED | Deleted and replaced. |\n| FROZEN | Skipped entirely. Position held fixed and treated as an obstacle by the generator. |\n| DETACHED | Generator prompts user: \"X objects have manual edits. Keep edits (freeze) or regenerate?\" |\n\n**State transitions:**\n\n| From | Event | To |\n|---|---|---|\n| (none) | Generator creates | GENERATED |\n| (none) | User draws directly | AUTHORED |\n| GENERATED | User edits geometry or parameters | DETACHED |\n| GENERATED | User explicitly freezes | FROZEN |\n| DETACHED | User explicitly freezes | FROZEN |\n| DETACHED | User accepts regeneration | (deleted, replaced by new GENERATED) |\n| FROZEN | User unfreezes | GENERATED (re-evaluated on next regeneration) |\n\n**Mental model:** authored objects are constraints; generated objects are\nconsequences. Moving a constraint freely updates its consequences. FROZEN and\nDETACHED are user-facing escape hatches when the automatic consequence is\nnot what the user wants.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Users can safely tweak generated layouts without fear of silent overwrite.\n- The generator always knows what it owns vs what is user-controlled.\n- Warnings are targeted (only DETACHED objects trigger prompts), not blanket.\n- \"Regenerate all\" is a safe, predictable operation with explicit exceptions.\n- Moving an AUTHORED road automatically updates dependent GENERATED yards\n  without any lock/unlock ceremony.\n\n## What this makes harder\n\n- Implementation has to maintain state transitions correctly across\n  regeneration, manual edit, freeze, and unfreeze operations.\n- Undo/redo must handle ownership state transitions as part of the history.\n- When displaying an object, the UI must show its ownership state clearly\n  (badge or outline style) so users know what kind of object they are\n  interacting with.\n","numLines":93,"startLine":1,"totalLines":93}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5962cbbf-f4be-43a5-8ae3-e45eb595339f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}

RTG_BLOCK\n\n**Version:** 1.0.0\n\nA rubber-tyred gantry container stack block. The primary storage element in\na container terminal yard.\n\n## Inputs\n\n### Geometry\n\n| Field | Type | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| `geometry.length_m` | number | Along the bay axis (RTG travel direction) |\n| `geometry.width_m` | number | Across bay, derived from zone configuration |\n| `geometry.bay_axis_p1` | Point2D | Project-local metric start of bay axis |\n| `geometry.bay_axis_p2` | Point2D | Project-local metric end of bay axis |\n\n### Parameters\n\n| Field | Type | Default | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `containers_wide` | integer | 6 | Number of container columns across bay (nw). Valid: 5, 6, 7 |\n| `stack_height` | integer | 5 | Containers in vertical stack (nh). Valid: 4, 5, 6 |\n| `rows` | integer | 1 | Single (1) or back-to-back (2) |\n| `rtg_type` | enum | `cantilever` | `cantilever` \\| `portal` |\n| `leg_strip_m` | number | 1.2 | RTG leg provision width (metres) |\n| `truck_lane_m` | number | 6.0 | Truck lane width (metres) |\n| `container_length_m` | number | 6.058 | CL_M, ISO 20ft container length |\n| `container_width_m` | number | 2.438 | CW_M, ISO 20ft container width |\n| `container_height_m` | number | 2.591 | CH_M, ISO 20ft container height |\n| `rtg_spacing_m` | number | 60.0 | Along-bay spacing between RTG positions |\n\n## `stack_capacity_teu` | number | TEU | `teu_slots × stack_height` |\n| `gross_area_m2` | number | m² | `length_m × cross_section_width_m` |\n| `net_container_area_m2` | number | m² | `length_m × (rows × containers_wide × container_width_m)` |\n| `truck_lane_length_m` | number | m | `length_m` (one-sided truck lane) |\n| `rtg_count` | number | units | `ceil(length_m / rtg_spacing_m)` |\n| `crane_positions` | number | positions | `rtg_count × 2` |\n| `cross_section_width_m` | number | m | Computed from zone layout (see below) |\n| `clearance_height_m` | number | m | `(stack_height + 1) × container_height_m + 2.0` |\n\n### Cross-section width computation\n\nFor `rtg_type = cantilever`:\n\n```\ncross_section_width_m =\n  truck_lane_m\n  + leg_strip_m\n  + (rows × containers_wide × container_width_m)\n  + leg_strip_m\n```\n\nFor `rtg_type = portal`:\n\n```\ncross_section_width_m =\n  leg_strip_m\n  + truck_lane_m\n  + (rows × containers_wide × container_width_m)\n  + leg_strip_m\n```\n\n## Validation rules\n\n| Rule ID | Scope | Severity | Condition |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `RTG_BLOCK_LENGTH_MAX` | OBJECT | WARNING | `length_m > 250` |\n| `RTG_BLOCK_LENGTH_MIN` | Assumptions and scope clarifications\n\nAnswered via pre-plan user decisions and Codex second-opinion review:\n\n| # | Question | Decision |\n|---|---|---|\n| 1 | Store placement | **Two-package split per ADR-015**: `packages/project-store` (vanilla Zustand + zundo + Immer, no React) and `packages/project-store-react` (React hooks wrapping project-store). No Load dropdown, no project enumeration UI. |\n| 4 | zundo scope | **Project slice only** per ADR-015. Selection, active tool, viewport — out of undo history. Not yet applicable in M1.2 (no canvas, no ephemeral UI state). |\n\nOther assumptions:\n\n- Persistence caller lives in `apps/web/src/persistence/` per ADR-014\n  (M1 client-side persistence; server + Postgres + PostGIS ships M3+).\n- IndexedDB wrapper: `idb` library (ADR-014 default).\n- Zod is the schema-validation library per ADR-012.\n- UUIDv7 via the `uuid` npm package (v11+ supports v7 natively).\n- `packages/domain` remains pure: no React, no Zustand, no IndexedDB.\n  Only types, Zod schemas, UUID generator, canonical-JSON serializer,\n  and pure logic.\n\n## 3. Planners draw port infrastructure in 2D.\nThe system extracts operational quantities from the geometry, runs validation\nand throughput analysis, computes capex and revenue, and reports inconsistencies\nback to the geometry layer. 3D is a derived view for spatial validation and\npresentation.\n\nIt is not a drawing tool. It is not a simulator. It is not a costing spreadsheet.\nThose tools already exist. This platform closes the loop between them.\n\n## The core loop\n\n```\ngeometry → quantity extraction → equipment derivation → operational parameters\n  → throughput + capex + revenue → validation → back to geometry as constraint\n```\n\nEvery architectural decision is evaluated against this loop. Does the decision\nmake the loop cleaner, faster, more auditable, more interactive? If not, it is\ndeprioritised.\n\n## What is authoritative vs derived\n\n**Authoritative:** the 2D project. Object geometry, classification,\nparameters, and ownership state. Nothing else is source of truth.\n\n**Derived:** extracted quantities, operational analysis, cost computations,\nvalidation results, 3D scene, visual projections on the basemap. All of these\nare deterministic functions of the authoritative document plus scenario\noverrides and library rates.\n\n## Scope\n\n**In scope:** port topside layout — roads, pavements, buildings, container\nstacks (RTG blocks), berth lines, gate complexes, utility corridors, and the\nthroughput/capex/revenue analysis derived from them.\n\n**Deferred:** vessel traffic modelling, bathymetric analysis, tidal modelling,\ntemporal phasing of construction, external API, real-time multi-user editing,\ngeometry branching across scenarios.\n\n**Out of scope:** navigational channel design, marine structural engineering,\ngeotechnical analysis, detailed MEP design.\n\n## Why it matters\n\nEvery port planner today works with AutoCAD plus Excel plus a capex spreadsheet\nplus a throughput model in another tool. None of these talk to each other. A\nlayout change in AutoCAD does not propagate to the capex estimate. A capacity\nassumption in the throughput model does not validate against the yard geometry.\nThe result is that plans are internally inconsistent, slow to iterate, and\npainful to audit.\n\nThis platform closes that loop. The primary differentiation over existing tools\nis not better drawing. It is the fact that the system can say \"your RTG block\nexceeds the 250m operational maximum\" or \"your throughput target requires 45%\nmore ground slots than your yard provides\" — and it can say it the moment the\nlayout changes, not weeks later.\n","numLines":62,"startLine":1,"totalLines":62}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a29ef80f-16d6-4b53-9566-9e7f1fa92e12","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"D:\\PortPlanner","sessionId":"cbe7ab7d-96ab-4f8b-8241-12b9cb14b062","version":"2.1.111","gitBranch":"main"}
